1933.01.12

Japanese Troops Retreat from Koumenkou

Zheng Guilin's Troops Flank the Enemy's Rear

Our Troops Occupy High Ground, Making It Difficult for the Enemy to Succeed

Several Sections of the Great Wall Destroyed by Enemy Bombardment

The Situation in Qinhuangdao Is Critical

(Beiping) The Japanese army has launched another attack on Koumenkou. At the same time, enemy traces have been discovered in Shimen Village and Lijia Fort, with fierce fighting occurring. Our troops are in a difficult situation. After our reinforcements arrived, they launched a head-on attack. Simultaneously, 3,000 troops from the volunteer army led by Zheng Guilin launched from Shihegou to flank the enemy at Lijia Fort. The enemy collapsed and concentrated in Wanjia Village, turning the situation from danger to safety for our army. Zheng's troops are currently engaged in fierce fighting with the Japanese at Gaoling. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) At 11:00 PM last night, the Japanese army's Miyake unit, consisting of field artillery, attacked our positions in two directions. One route attacked Koumenkou from Wanjia Village outside the pass, and the other route pressed Shimen Village from the Liujiang River. After resistance from a certain regiment of the 0th Brigade, the enemy fired over 200 shells, destroying several sections of the Great Wall at Koumenkou. On the morning of the 11th, the enemy dispatched five aircraft to assist in the bombing. Our soldiers stationed at Koumenkou and Shimen Village are willing to coexist with the city and are determined to defend it to the death. Their morale is high, and fierce fighting is ongoing. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) Yesterday morning, the main force of the Japanese army, under the cover of aircraft, attacked Koumenkou. Our troops fought bravely, and the fighting was fierce. There have been no changes to the Shihe Line. Enemy aircraft scouted and dropped bombs in the area of Fudian and Haiyang Town, east and west of the Shihe River. No enemy aircraft have been seen over Qinhuangdao for three days. Last night, the lights suddenly went out at the Yuguan Railway Station and the Beining Railway Factory, and locomotives were being moved back and forth, reportedly due to the Japanese army mobilizing troops or other intentions. Qinhuangdao is being maintained by a certain unit. Tao has assumed the concurrent post of Linyu County Magistrate, and the county government is temporarily located in a certain place. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) A Japanese warship anchored at Qinhuangdao sailed away on the morning of the 9th. A destroyer patrolled the sea area in front of Yuguan, Suizhong, and other areas. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) The telephone line between Beiping and Qinhuangdao experienced a temporary disruption due to excessive wind force after 3:00 PM yesterday. It was restored that evening. This morning, the line was unclear again due to strong winds. Qinhuangdao has suddenly become tense since the Japanese marines landed. Stores that had reopened have closed again. Our armored vehicles are still stationed outside the port, guarding the railway. There is no fighting on the Shihe front line. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) The battle at Koumenkou is extremely fierce. The Japanese army stationed in Yuguan transferred 300 troops last night to reinforce Koumenkou. Detailed battle situation is unknown. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Linyu: After the enemy retreated from Koumenkou to Lijia Fort, more than a hundred puppet police officers harassed the area on the 11th, from morning to night. Although there were occasional gunshots from the enemy, there was no intense warfare. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Linyu: Two trains carrying infantry and artillery departed from Yuguan Station on the evening of the 11th for Wanjia Village to attack Koumenkou. There are rumors that Japanese warships in Qinhuangdao are scheduled to bombard Qinhuangdao's streets on the 12th. There are currently three Japanese warships and two Japanese merchant ships in the area, fully loaded with ammunition for supplies, which are being unloaded gradually. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qinhuangdao telegram: This morning, our forward sentry captured an enemy spy, who was immediately sent to headquarters. According to the confession, the Japanese plan is to first attack Koumenkou, because after the Japanese army occupied Yuguan, they planned to cut off our defense line from Yuguan to Koumenkou. With the discovery of the Japanese plot, He Zhuguo immediately ordered his troops to be on strict guard. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) The situation in Qinhuangdao is very tense. The Japanese army's defense line is only 300 meters away from the railway. At night, naval warships shine searchlights on the city. The 5th Regiment of Gu Yi, stationed in Dongluocheng, Yuguan, moved about 200 troops towards Jiaoshan, fifteen li northeast of Yuguan, on the morning of the 10th, with the intention of threatening our army at Koumenkou. Today, the Japanese army on the Shihe front has not taken any action. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) The volunteer army led by Zheng Guilin has been attacking the Japanese army's rear lines outside the pass for several consecutive days. Since the Yuguan Incident, there has been contact every day. On January 2nd, they attacked the vanguard in Qian'suo. On the 3rd, they attacked the vanguard of Qian'suo, Gaoling, and Suizhong. On the 4th, they attacked Majiayingzi and broke Er'dong. On the 5th, they attacked Qianyin'zhang and Koumentai. On the 6th, they attacked Tie'ertai. On the 7th, they attacked Lijia Fort. On the 8th, they attacked Tieling Fort. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Tianjin) After the enemy occupied Yuguan, fearing that our army would exit Koumenkou and cut off their communication, the Suzuki Brigade sent a regiment north. They made contact with our army on the 7th and were repelled. The enemy then reinforced with one regiment each of infantry and cavalry, and one company of artillery, and attacked in three routes. A conflict occurred on the morning of the 10th, with exceptionally intense artillery fire. The Japanese News Agency publicized that the Japanese army had completely occupied it by 9:00 AM on the 10th, which is completely untrue. On the evening of the 11th, reporters inquired with the Japanese military headquarters stationed in Tianjin. According to them, as of 6:00 PM on the 11th, fighting was still ongoing and they had not received any reports of occupation. There were also conflicts in Shimen Village. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The transportation sector received a telegram from the Tianjin Telegraph Bureau stating that the Japanese army attacked Koumenkou again on the 11th. Our army has received considerable reinforcements, morale is extremely high, and the enemy has made no progress. The Japanese are claiming in Beiping and Tianjin that they have occupied Koumenkou, which is absolutely untrue. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The government has never considered the Japanese army's forcible occupation of Yuguan a local issue, but rather as part of the entire Sino-Japanese problem. Recently, the situation in the Qinhuangdao area has become serious, and the Japanese army has begun to attack the strategic pass of Koumenkou. In order to understand the actual situation on the ground, the government has specially dispatched Vice Minister Liu Chongjie to the north to inspect and discuss everything with Zhang. After the matter is completed, he will return to Beijing to report. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Japanese army continued to launch a fierce attack on Koumenkou yesterday and today, and the battle was very fierce. Our defending troops are a cavalry brigade. Japanese aircraft repeatedly arrived in Qinhuangdao to distribute propaganda, claiming that the Japanese army had occupied Koumenkou. The local residents are well aware of the Japanese people's habitual techniques of spreading rumors and were not moved by them. The Koumenkou area has suddenly become cold. Our army occupies a high position, making it very difficult for the Japanese army to attack. Japanese casualties are high, and many mules and horses have been abandoned. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Righteous Army of the North China National Salvation Association sends a telegram to He Zhuguo and Zhu Qing to express condolences. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Tianjin) According to a certain military expert, Koumenkou and Shimen Village have undulating hills and rugged roads. The terrain is dangerous and strategically important, making it a place that has been contested by military strategists since ancient times. It is easy to defend but difficult to attack. However, our army has troops stationed in both places. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Tianjin) It is rumored in Beiping that the Qinhuangdao Telephone Bureau and Telegraph Bureau have been occupied by Japanese soldiers. Reporters investigated with the transportation authorities and found that this is completely untrue. The area is peaceful. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Tianjin) There is no intense fighting in Shihe either. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) There will be several days of quiet on all fronts. This is not the result of negotiations, but rather due to the weather. There are currently strong winds in North China, which are as sharp as scissors, making it impossible for battles to take place. Chinese authorities still claim that Koumenkou has not been lost. Upon investigation, the Koumenkou fortress is two miles long, and what the Chinese soldiers are guarding appears to be the south entrance, but the north entrance has already been sealed off by the Japanese army. (Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

(Beiping) The British and American embassies have now received a telegram from China protesting to the signatories of the 1901 treaty, opposing Japan's illegal use of the Beining Railway to attack and occupy Yuguan. (Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

(Beiping) According to travelers who arrived here from Yuguan, the city is gradually returning to normal. Many shops have reopened, and civilians are returning home one after another. Japanese flags are hanging everywhere, and the entire city is patrolled by Japanese soldiers. The damage suffered by Yuguan was mostly due to artillery fire. It is said that most of the damage was within a hundred yards of the South Gate, and the South Gate has been destroyed. (Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

(Qinhuangdao) A special Reuters correspondent here learned today that a Manchu detective was executed by order of General He Zhuguo. The correspondent traveled to the cavalry brigade of the Chinese army's northern front line, ten miles north of Qinhuangdao. The brigade commander told the correspondent in his headquarters that there is currently a large unit of the Japanese army in Yuguan, carrying tanks and artillery. They have not shown any signs of attacking for days. There are currently pseudo-Manchukuo troops in Koumenkou, including about one hundred cavalry and some infantry. The Chinese army's front line reaches Shimen'an in the north and the coast in the south. After returning to Qinhuangdao, the correspondent visited the Chinese army's front line south of the railway and saw that General He Zhuguo's deployment was very thorough, but the defense area was very large, and the troops were weak. It is feared that it would be difficult to resist the fierce attack of a large number of well-equipped enemy troops. (Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

Japanese Aircraft Bomb Various Areas in Jehol

Thirty-Five Trains Carrying Japanese Soldiers Depart from Shenyang

The Japanese Side Decides to Instigate Pseudo-State Troops to Invade Jehol

(Beiping) The enemy's plan to seize Jehol is becoming more urgent. They are busy increasing troops and transporting weapons every day. The enemy and the Righteous Army only have small-scale contact every day and have not yet formally invaded. Our army is on strict alert. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) Japanese aircraft scouted over Chengde, Chaoyang, Beipiao, and other places yesterday and began to bomb various key points on the Suizhong-Lingyuan highway. Pingquan, Boli Mountain, Wohutun, Dingmatang, and other places were all destroyed by Japanese aircraft. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) Thirty-five trains carrying Japanese soldiers departed from Shenyang on the 9th, most of them disembarked at Goubangzi, Dahushan, and Jin County, and advanced towards Fuxin and Suidong in northern Jehol. Among these trains, fifteen were troops of the pseudo-Manchukuo, led by former Zhili-Shandong United Army division commander Fang Yongchang. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) Tang Yulin telegraphed the Ministry of Military Affairs yesterday, stating that according to reports, Japan and the pseudo-state will invade Jehol and disrupt the situation in Beiping and Tianjin around the time of the Lunar New Year. In light of the previous sacrifices in Shanghai and the international criticism, Japan has decided to use pseudo-state troops to invade Jehol and use bandit troops composed of frustrated soldiers and reactionary soldiers to disrupt the situation in Beiping and Tianjin, with the Japanese directing from behind. He vowed to serve the country with his life. If the Japanese invade, he will launch a head-on attack, regardless of success or failure. He only requests that the national forces provide assistance. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Central Political Council Approves List of Third Legislative Yuan Members

Cases Submitted by the Third Plenary Session to Be Reviewed by Various Groups

Regulations on Aviation and Highway Construction Lottery Bonds Passed

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its 339th meeting on the morning of the 11th. The meeting was attended by members Yu Youren, Ye Chucang, Sun Ke, Lin Sen, He Yingqin, Chen Gongbo, Shi Qingyang, Shi Ying, Liang Hancao, Wu Tiecheng, Liu Shouzhong, Zhu Jiahua, Luo Jialun, He Yaozu, Huang Musong, Bai Yunti, Ke Xing'e, Zhang Zhi'fan, Yang Hu, Tang Youren, Wang Qi, Miao Peicheng, Li Ciwen, Fang Juehui, Zheng Zhannan, Zhao Pilian, Gu Zhenggang, Zhang Qun, and over thirty other people. Yu Youren chaired the meeting. The following important cases were discussed:

(1) Cases submitted by the Third Plenary Session: (A) Reform of Education Plan Case, to be reviewed by the Education Group; (B) Relief of Unemployed Overseas Chinese Case, to be drafted by the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee to formulate practical measures and submitted to the Council for review; (C) Reduction of Provincial Areas Case, to be reviewed jointly by the Political Report Group, Legal Group, Finance Group, and Military Group; (D) Establishment of Research Associations by Party, Government, and Military Agencies Case, to be handled by the Political Report Group; (E) Establishment of a Design Committee of the National Government Case,

to be handled by the Political Report Group; (F) Unification of Judicial Expenses Case, to be handled by the Political Report Group and the Finance Group; (G) Prohibition of Artificial Fertilizers Case, to be handled by the Executive Yuan.

(2) The Executive Yuan submitted a report from the Ministry of Finance on developing aviation and building highways, requesting approval to hold aviation and highway construction lottery bonds and submitting the lottery bond regulations for approval. Resolution: Passed.

(3) The Legal and Education Groups reported on the review of the Examination Law, Examination Supervision Law, and the organizational law principles of the Examination Committee. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinions and submitted to the Legislative Yuan.

(4) The Legal and Education Groups reported on the review of the proposal submitted by Committee Member Dai Fu-xian on matters that should be promoted or reformed regarding various administrative systems related to examinations. They believed that the principles were generally acceptable. The National Government should first forward them to various agencies for comments and then submit them to the Examination Yuan to formulate concrete plans.

(5) The Education and Finance Groups reported on the review of the proposal submitted by Committee Member Liu Zhi on establishing a Henan Museum. They advocated expanding the existing Henan Museum, and the central government should send a letter to all Boxer Indemnity committees to consider providing subsidies.

(6) Member and President of the Legislative Yuan Sun Ke proposed to appoint Ma Yinchu, Fu Bingchang, Lu Zhiyi, Jiao Yitang, Shi Shangkuan, Lin Bin, Chen Zhaoying, Ma Chaojun, Liu Zixun, Peng Yangguang, Dai Xiujun, Lou Zisun, Wu Shangying, Feng Zhaoyi, Zhang Zhibiao, Tao Xuan, Feng Zhaoyin, Chen Changheng, Lu Zhonglin, Zhang Fengjiu, Fang Juehui, Liu Jixue, Luo Ding, Cai Xuan, Wei Tingsheng, Liu Keli, Liu Jingxin, Zhu Hezhong, Shi Weihuan, Zhu Lisu, Huang Youchang, Ma Chaojun, Zhu Jingsong, Zheng Kaichen, Fu Rulin, Zhang Weihan, Jia Shiyi, Li Zhonggong, Di Ying, Cheng Zhonghang, He Sui, Ding Chaowu, Deng Jiayan, Zhang Zhiben, Huang Jilu, Liang Hancao, Pan Yunchao, Tang Youren, Huang Fusheng, Wang Qi, Wang Bingqian, Dai Ren, Feng Ziyou, Xu Yuangao, Zhang Guoyuan, Huang Yiou, Liu Tong, Deng Zhexi, Wang Kunlun, Deng Hongye, Wang Shufang, Deng Gongxuan, Wu Jingxiong, Qu Cengze, Zhao Chen, Sheng Zhenwei, Chen Ruxuan, Luo Yunyan, Chen Bozhuang, Yao Chuanfa, Sun Weilian, Qi Zhihou, Chen Junpu, Wang Zenshan, Chen Jianru, Tao Luqian, Jian Youwen, Zhong Tianxin, Wang Xiaoying, Hu Xuanming, Wang Yuxiang, Yang Gongda, Xie Shoukang, Dong Qizheng, Zhou Yizhi, Zhao Wenbing, Di Luwa, Bokjijiya, Gongjue Zhongni, and Losang Jianzan, ninety people in total, as members of the Third Legislative Yuan. Resolution: Passed.

(7) Supervisory Committee Member Wang Shiduo of the Control Yuan resigned. Approved. (8) The National Government retroactively appointed Shi Zhaoji as the Special Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary to the United States. (Central News Agency, 10th)

(Nanjing) The list of the Third Legislative Yuan, totaling ninety members, was approved by the Central Political Council on the 11th. The First Legislative Yuan had forty-nine members, and the Second Legislative Yuan had sixty-three members. Forty-one members of the Second Legislative Yuan were re-elected. Twenty-one members, including Zhang Mojun, Li Shuhua, and Soong Mei-ling, were not re-elected. (Central News Agency, 11th)

Sun Ke Scheduled to Take Office Next Monday

Will Visit the Yuan Today to Handle Affairs

Liang Hancao to be Appointed Secretary-General

(Nanjing) The list of members of the Third Legislative Yuan has been approved by the Central Political Council on the 11th and will be officially appointed by the National Government. It is reported that all members and President Sun will be sworn in simultaneously after the next National Government Memorial Week. Sun is scheduled to handle affairs on the morning of the 12th, and the first meeting will also be held within the next week. (Central News Agency, 11th)

(Nanjing) Secretary-General of the Legislative Yuan Zhang Weihan resigned, and Liang Hancao is slated to succeed him. The Director of the Translation Bureau is slated to be Wu Shangying. As for the chairpersons of various committees, Jiao Yitang will serve as Chairperson of the Legal Committee, Ma Yinchu will serve as Chairperson of the Economic Committee, Deng Shiyin will serve as Chairperson of the Finance Committee, Fu Bingchang will serve as Chairperson of the Foreign Affairs Committee, and Chen Zhaoying will serve as Chairperson of the Military Affairs Committee. (Central News Agency, 11th)

He Zhuguo Denies Reports of the Fall of Koumenkou

(Beiping) He Zhuguo telegraphed Beiping this morning, stating that the Japanese attack on Koumenkou was repeatedly repelled by our army. Foreign reports that Koumenkou fell yesterday are absolutely untrue. Koumenkou is still being defended by our 0th Brigade, relying on the terrain. At 9:00 AM yesterday, Japanese cavalry attacked Koumenkou from Wanjia Village, and fierce fighting occurred with our army at Jihua Ridge. Both sides suffered heavy casualties. Our army, relying on the natural barrier and occupying the high ground, repelled three attacks by a large force of Japanese troops supervising pseudo-state troops. Our army poured water on the slopes of Koumenkou to create ice, making it difficult for the Japanese army to advance. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Japanese Government Responds to China's Protest

Counter-Accuses Our Army of Provocation

(Tokyo) The Chinese government previously lodged a protest with Japan regarding the Yuguan case. The Japanese government has now sent a reply to the Japanese Ambassador to China, Arima. It is expected to be delivered to the Chinese government today. The letter still claims that the battle was caused by Chinese military provocation and that China should be responsible. Japan currently reserves the right to demand regarding this case.

(Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

(Nanjing) The Japanese occupied Yuguan, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs lodged a serious protest.

Japan has repeatedly promised to respond to this protest letter, but they have been fabricating facts, which has caused considerable delays. As of the 11th, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had not yet received it. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Chiang Kai-shek Discusses Diplomatic Events with Key Figures

North China Generals All Willing to Advance Bravely

(Nanjing) Because Yuguan has fallen and Jehol is in danger, Chiang Kai-shek privately invited Soong Tzu-wen, He Yingqin, Luo Wengan, and Chen Lifu to his private residence in the Mausoleum Park on the morning of the 11th to discuss important matters. It is reported that they discussed the situation on the front lines, foreign policy, and the situation in the League of Nations, and exchanged opinions. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) A certain representative from North China who came to Beijing said that the generals in North China have realized since the fall of Yuguan that the only way out is to unite sincerely and strive to resist under the guidance of the central government. Currently, all generals and subordinates are willing to advance bravely and win back national dignity. Their only slogan is not to let the 19th Route Army have all the glory. They hope that the government will quickly establish a resistance plan so that soldiers in various places can provide practical assistance and the central government will stop making empty promises. (Eleventh Dispatch)

An De-xin's Remains Buried in Qinhuangdao

(Beiping) An De-xin's remains did not arrive in Beiping yesterday. It is reported that An's coffin was transported to Qinhuangdao and buried there according to Islamic customs. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Two Japanese Aircraft Collide Outside Harbin

Pilots Killed

(Harbin) Two Japanese aircraft collided with each other during landing outside this city today. Both aircraft were destroyed, and both pilots were killed. (Tenth Dispatch, Reuters)

Wang Jingwei Departs from Germany to Return Home

(Berlin) Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan of China, went to Speyer, Germany for medical treatment due to illness. Due to the Yuguan Incident, he is extremely worried and decided to return home as soon as possible, even though he has not fully recovered. He departed from Speyer today and will return to China by ship from Marseille. (Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

Stuttgart: Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan of China, suddenly left the hospital in Speyer this morning due to the serious situation in the Far East. According to reliable private sources, Wang decided to return early because he had received repeated telegrams from the National Government in recent days requesting him to return home quickly. However, it is expected that Wang will first travel to Geneva before boarding a ship to return to Shanghai, where he will discuss the Manchurian case with Chinese representatives or representatives of major powers. It is still unknown whether he will stay in Geneva temporarily until the Committee of Nineteen convenes. (Eleventh Dispatch, Guomin News Agency)

Speyer: After receiving an urgent telegram from China, Wang Qingwei, President of the Executive Yuan of China, left the tropical disease hospital early. He left Speyer with his doctors today and will go to a certain health resort in Germany for a short period of convalescence before returning home. He is expected to return to China around March. (Eleventh Dispatch, Guomin News Agency)

Luo Wengan Dispatches Liu Chongjie to the North

To Discuss Foreign Affairs with Zhang Xueliang

(Nanjing) Luo Wengan dispatched Vice Minister Liu Chongjie to Beiping to meet with Zhang Xueliang and discuss foreign affairs issues. Liu crossed the river to the north on the evening of the 11th. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Liu Chongjie, Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, went north today after paying visits to Chiang Kai-shek, Soong Tzu-wen, and others for instructions. Liu travelled frequently for discussions. This trip north is investigatory in nature and has no other tasks. He will first go to Beiping to meet with Zhang, convey the central government's intentions, and report on foreign policy. After completing this, he will travel to Tianjin, Qinhuangdao, and various locations on the front line for inspection. He is expected to return to Beijing in about two weeks. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Liu Chongjie is taking a train to Beiping tonight. Official circles are unwilling to announce his mission, but it is reported that Liu will inform Zhang Xueliang in detail of the government's attitude towards the Yuguan case. It is widely believed that having a responsible representative of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stationed in Beiping will be beneficial to the matter. It is reported that Liu will remain in Beiping until the situation in North China eases. The government considers the Yuguan incident to be part of the entire Sino-Japanese problem and cannot be treated as a local incident to be resolved locally. (Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

Shenyang Pseudo-Army Guerrillas Revolt

(Beiping) A certain regiment of the Shenyang Jing'an Guerrilla Force was ordered last week to attack Deng Tie-mei's troops, led by a certain Japanese lieutenant colonel and twenty Japanese soldiers. After arriving in Fengcheng, the guerrillas in the Third District suddenly fired into the sky to signal the Righteous Army. The Japanese army then ordered the Jing'an Force to return to Shenyang and planned to punish them. The Jing'an Force then held a secret meeting, eliminated all the Japanese, and surrendered with all their weapons to Deng Tie-mei's troops to join the anti-Japanese struggle. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Li Zongren Arrives in Guangzhou

To Discuss Anti-Enemy Measures with Chen Jitang

(Hong Kong) Li Zongren, accompanied by Dan Maoxin, Zhang Yaguang, and Gan Jiayi, arrived in the province at 10:00 AM on the 11th. Li said that to resist the Japanese invasion of Yuguan, the entire country's military force must be used to recover the lost territory. If the central government has already decided on an overall plan, Guangxi can dispatch troops at any time. But Zhang said that after representing Guizhou to contact Guangdong, he will go to Guizhou and then return to Guizhou. Gan said that he would report on the Guizhou changes to the Xiangzheng Council and request that efforts be made to mediate. In the afternoon, Li visited Chen Jitang to discuss ways to deal with Japan: 1. Jointly telegram the central government to quickly decide on a grand strategy, vowing to resist Japan to the death to save the national soul; 2. Telegram the generals in North China to leave the pass and kill the enemy, and request the assistance of the generals of Jin, Hebei, Chahar, and Sui; the 14th Group Army is willing to be the support; 3. Earnestly strengthen national defense, expand military preparations, firmly defend fortresses, and build artillery forts; 4. Order the Guangdong and Guangxi armies to concentrate and be on standby, dispatching troops to resist Japan. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Chen Jitang went to Yiyang Garden on the 11th to visit Li Yangjing, who is ill. Yu Hanmou is allowed to return to the province within three days. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) Li Zongren arrived here from Wuzhou today, accompanied by representatives from Guizhou. Official circles welcomed them as required. Li told a Reuters reporter that he will discuss Southwest national defense issues with the Guangdong authorities. He believes that force is the only way to solve the Sino-Japanese problem. He advocates national mobilization and fighting the invaders. (Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

(Guangzhou) The Guangdong Provincial Government is now starting to reorganize government personnel in order to implement the three-year plan. All government agencies must record in detail the education, experience, and other qualifications of their staff. Starting next year, anyone who does not meet the qualifications will be dismissed, so that public affairs can be handled by capable people and measures can be taken smoothly. (Eleventh Dispatch, Reuters)

Yan, Gu, and Guo, Three Representatives, Telegraph Request for Troops to Recover Yuguan

"We Can Help Ourselves, and the League of Nations and Other Countries Can Begin to Help Us"

(Geneva) The three representatives, Yan, Gu, and Guo, telegraphed the government today, stating briefly, Shanhaiguan is the key to the northern gate, please quickly send troops to recover it, and said that we can help ourselves, and the League of Nations and friendly countries can begin to help us. (Eleventh Dispatch, Central News Agency)

League of Nations Mediation of Sino-Japanese Case Offers Little Hope

Preparing to Draft Report

Forcing Both Sides to Accept

Still Trying to Avoid Direct Conflict with Japan

(Geneva) A Sino-Japanese settlement is now generally considered hopeless. Those directing League of Nations policy behind the scenes are busy planning the course to be taken when the Committee of Nineteen meets next week. It now seems inevitable that the next step will be to apply Section 4 of Article 15 of the League Covenant, which stipulates that "if the dispute is not settled, the Council, either unanimously or by majority vote, shall prepare a report stating the facts of the dispute and the recommendations which are deemed just and proper by the Council." It is widely understood that there is little possibility of using delaying tactics to seek repeated postponements. Therefore, serious consideration is being given to the drafting of a report that the League Assembly must prepare. It is said that there is a trend to adopt the draft resolution of the Committee of Nineteen and its explanatory memorandum as the basis for the report, with appropriate revisions. This is to base the solution on the proposals of the Lytton Report. It is hoped that this outline can be used to draft a report that expresses the will of the League member states in a careful manner, while avoiding a break with Japan. However, Japan seems unlikely to accept the general endorsement of the Lytton Report, and China will also demand a solution that at least allows it freedom of action. Japanese chief delegate Matsuoka, recently touring the Near East and Italy, will return to Geneva tomorrow. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic circles, Yan Huiqing, Gu Weijun, and Guo Qinqi have all arrived in Geneva and reported by telegram that they are awaiting the outcome of the meeting of the Committee of Nineteen. They will then observe the proceedings of the Committee of Nineteen, and if mediation proves hopeless, they will draft a report based on the Covenant, proposing a solution and forcing both sides to accept it. If either party refuses to accept, economic sanctions will be imposed. Our representatives have repeatedly submitted to the League of Nations reports on the Japanese military occupation of Shanhaiguan and the expansion of Japanese war actions. At the same time, they have also submitted a written request to the League of Nations, urging it to pay attention to its own responsibilities and promptly stop Japan's expanding military actions to avoid endangering world peace, and to order Japan to withdraw its troops as soon as possible in accordance with the League of Nations resolutions and restore the situation before September 18. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Amidst Rumors, Residents of Beiping Seek Refuge

Income of the Beiping-Hankou Railway Increases Sharply

(Beiping) Since the Yu Pass Incident, families of high officials and wealthy merchants in Beiping have been moving to Tianjin, Hankou and other places. The eastern and western railway stations are piled high with luggage, and revenues have increased sharply. The Beining Railway has increased its daily income by more than ten thousand yuan, and the Beiping-Hankou Railway has increased its daily income by more than twenty thousand yuan.

(Beiping) Trains on the Beining and Beipingpu lines arriving in Beiping are now delayed by one to two hours. The number of passengers has been extremely crowded in recent days. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Severe Cold and Snow

Snow in the Capital Nanjing and Wuhan

Severe Cold in Beiping and Jinan

(Nanjing) The weather turned cold on the eleventh, with the temperature dropping to thirty-two degrees, a difference of more than twenty degrees from yesterday. There was light snow in the morning and afternoon, and a howling wind and heavy snow in the evening, which continued into the night. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The climate in the capital city was still mild as winter approached. It only began to snow slightly on the third day and gradually turned cold, but then it warmed up again. On the ninth, the sun shone brightly, like a second spring. On the tenth, the weather changed with strong winds and light rain. On the morning of the eleventh, snow fell, with a howling northwest wind and extreme cold. (Eleventh Dispatch from the Central News Agency)

(Hankou) There was heavy snow in Wuhan on the eleventh, and the weather turned cold. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Beiping) Beiping is experiencing severe cold and strong winds today, with the outdoor temperature at minus sixteen degrees. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Jinan) It is extremely cold today, reaching minus eight degrees Celsius. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) Snow began in Xuzhou on the eleventh, promising well for the wheat seedlings and gradually dispelling the plague. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Current Commentary

How is the Reality of "Resistance"? 力

After encompassing our Northeast, the violent Japan brazenly disregards everything, advances to occupy Yu Pass, the national territory shrinks daily, and the national situation is in danger. People throughout the country are pained and indignant. Even those who previously advocated caution now seem to have changed their minds and advocate actual resistance to save our nation from its perilous state. Speeches by Zhang Xueliang, telegrams from Yan Xishan, Han Fuqu, and others, and even Liu Xiang, who is deeply involved in civil war, has stated that "the civil war will be ended and we will unite to resist foreign aggression." This can be said to be national unity. However, Yu Pass has been occupied for more than ten days, and in fact, the authorities' response to this incident is still nothing more than issuing protests to Japan and continuing to appeal to the League of Nations. So where is the so-called advocacy of actual resistance?

We believe that even a child of three feet tall is already clear about the current aggression of Japanese imperialism. It cannot be stopped by "protests" or even "serious protests." Their continental policy has been carefully considered and thoroughly planned. They brazenly disregard world opinion, and what more do they care about empty "protests?" The League of Nations itself is just a group of the strong. The facts of the past year can also prove that "justice" cannot be achieved by appeals. Even if we pour out our grievances again today, how can we be sure that it will be effective? Therefore, the only way to deal with today's situation is to "fight to the death" in order to "fight for survival," to "achieve justice," and to stop the violent actions of the imperialists. This is an undeniable truth. To talk about saving the country without this is empty talk.

The aggressive and violent actions of Japanese imperialism today are enough to shock the whole world. But on the other hand, our country's extreme concession and extreme endurance, being subjected to trampling without resistance, is also a rare sight in today's world. Only because we have extreme concession and endurance do we have such a brazen and reckless enemy. If our country had resisted desperately from the beginning of the September 18th Incident, it would not have been so reckless. Instead, we have endured and procrastinated, waiting to be slaughtered. We have been indifferent as if nothing had happened, and then we have begged others for help. The loss of Yu Pass today and the continuous advance of the Japanese army are the result of this. How can this be without reason?

Yesterday, this newspaper's Beiping correspondent reported that a foreign newspaper in the Northeast commented that "the Chinese nation is truly a lazy nation. The means adopted by Japan to deal with this kind of lazy nation are extremely correct. If these means were applied to any Western nation, there would not be a day of peace." Although their words are arrogant, the stones from other hills can be used to polish jade. We should also seriously consider this. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini said, "Words are beautiful, but guns are more beautiful." The humiliation that no country in the world can tolerate, the suffering that no one can endure, we want to solve everything with "words" such as protests and appeals. How can this be possible?

In short, today's situation is urgent and allows no further hesitation. The sun flag flying over Shanhaiguan may advance and fly over the city walls of Beijing at any time, even spreading throughout our country. There should be an end to endurance and a limit to concession. The people of the whole country are now looking to our government to show the facts. These facts are not "mediation," not "negotiation," not "protests," not "appeals," but actual action. What will happen to today's events?

No Change in US Far East Policy

After Roosevelt Meets with Stimson

Believes No Need to Reiterate at Present

(Washington) Secretary of State Stimson has completed his visit to New York to meet with President-elect Roosevelt and will return to Washington tonight. Political circles are well aware that Roosevelt refused to cooperate with Hoover. This meeting with Stimson was merely to inquire about the facts. Therefore, the general public is not paying much attention to this matter. It is said that Roosevelt generally agrees with Stimson's Far East policy, but believes that there is no need to reiterate the US view on the Far East at present. (Tenth Havas Dispatch)

▲Osaka Asahi Shimbun Washington Special Dispatch After the outbreak of the Yu Pass Incident, although the US State Department authorities were quite calm, the future development is indeed worrying. From the official American point of view, it is generally said that "American policy believes that Secretary of State Stimson has clearly stated in the note to Japan on January 7 last year and in the document submitted by Chairman of the Foreign Relations Committee Borah on February 4 that there will be no change in the original agreement in the future." From this, it can be inferred that the principle of not recognizing Manchukuo, even in the era of the next President Roosevelt, is unlikely to change the policy. Currently, the US government believes that if the Japanese army crosses the Great Wall and invades the Chinese mainland, it will inevitably cause major new problems for the peace treaty, and on the other hand, it will inevitably lead to disputes with the Soviet Union. The current Hoover administration lacks authority due to the imminent change of new and old, so there will be no action. For example, the issue of war debts, like the lack of progress in the Sino-Japanese issue, is because both Hoover and Roosevelt are unwilling to make positive decisions. Recently, Ambassador Debuchi visited Undersecretary of State Castle for the Yu Pass Incident, and the First Secretary of the Chinese Embassy visited Horiuchi, Director of the Far East Bureau. US officials are unwilling to express any opinions.

Hoover Proposes Arms Embargo to Congress

Original Bill Repeatedly Modified, Practically a Mere Formality

Sufficient to See the Power of Manufacturers to Control the Government

Geneva Convention Unlikely to be Ratified by the Senate

(Washington) US President Hoover today submitted to Congress a bill to ban the export of arms, but its content is no longer as originally intended by the State Department. The phrase "the President may prohibit exports at any time" has been amended to "the President may restrict the export of arms after obtaining the cooperation of other countries." Therefore, many in Congress say that this shows the power of American arms manufacturers to control national policy. After this amendment, the bill has little practical effect and is almost a mere formality. The US President also sent a special report urging the Senate to ratify the international convention on the prohibition of arms trafficking signed in Geneva on June 17, 1925, saying that if this convention cannot be ratified, then Congress must urgently pass a bill authorizing the President to prohibit the transportation of arms for military use after obtaining the cooperation of major arms manufacturing countries. In addition, he also attached a letter from Secretary of State Stimson to the President, the content of which was a suggestion that the President should ask Congress to authorize the government to prohibit the transportation of arms to warring countries in order to enhance the effectiveness of the Pact of Paris. This bill had been drafted by the State Department for a long time and shelved in the White House until it was submitted to Congress today. The reason why it was revised before being submitted to Congress was because of the opposition of certain cabinet members and arms manufacturers. It is rumored that one section was completely changed, and there were many other modifications, so members of Congress said that this bill would have little effect. After the bill was delivered to Congress, Senator Borah immediately stated that the Senate Foreign Relations Committee would consider the Geneva Convention tomorrow. The convention has been shelved in the Senate for several years and has not been voted on. However, according to Borah, the committee may not necessarily approve the convention. At the same time, Assistant Secretary of State Rogers also declared in the Senate Foreign Relations Committee that President-elect Roosevelt is still free to decide on the US plan to attend the international disarmament conference. The State Department has not accepted any constraints and has not agreed to its agenda. (Tenth National Dispatch)

US Senator Advocates Concluding a New International Treaty

Supporting the Stimson Doctrine

(Washington) US Senator King believes that the Kellogg-Briand Pact has little effect on maintaining world peace. Today, he specially submitted a resolution to the Senate requesting the conclusion of a new international treaty to support the US policy of not recognizing territories acquired by force. He advocated authorizing the President to negotiate international treaties to prohibit the use of force to seize territory in order to avoid wars. King's intention is to recognize that countries can conclude a treaty in which all territories acquired by undeclared wars or after declarations of war are illegal acts. According to King, a Democrat, this type of treaty will of course be handled by the Democratic government. (Tenth National Dispatch)

Britain Holds the Key to the Manchurian Case

Indecisive Attitude Toward Japan is Clearly Inappropriate

丨Cecil Publishes a Letter丨

(London) The Times this morning published a letter from Sir Cecil in an important position, stating that Britain holds the key to both the Manchurian and disarmament issues. The Yu Pass Incident shows the danger of a vacillating policy. The world hopes that the British side will provide clear and courageous guidance. He believes that if the League Assembly handles the matter courageously based on the Lytton Report, neither side would dare to disobey. But if one side disobeys, then the League members must consult with other countries. Cecil and Gray are chairmen of the British League of Nations Society. Cecil is known for his support of the League of Nations. (Eleventh Reuters Dispatch)

Japan Tries Hard to Win Over Britain

(Tokyo) According to diplomatic circles, Japan is focusing on Britain in its response to the Committee of Nineteen. It begs Britain to remember the old friendship of the Anglo-Japanese alliance in order to formulate a new plan favorable to Japan through an Anglo-Japanese compromise and to put pressure on the smaller countries. Therefore, it ordered Matsuoka not to tour Britain, but to return to Geneva early and work with Sugimura Yotaro to win over Drummond. Sugimura and Drummond have secretly negotiated several times, but have not achieved good results. Although Britain intends to favor Japan, it has not found suitable words to perfunctorily satisfy the world. In addition, the Yu Pass Incident has occurred, and the anger of European and American people against Japan is becoming more and more fierce. In order to maintain its reputation in Europe and the United States, Britain feels it is difficult to be friends with the violent Japan. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs is very anxious after hearing the news. (Eleventh China United News Dispatch)

Simon Arrives in Paris to Meet Pongou

(Paris) British Foreign Secretary Simon, who has been convalescing in Monte Carlo, unexpectedly arrived here today and met with French Prime Minister Pongou. At that time, the French cabinet was holding a meeting to discuss the budget. The meeting between the British and French politicians was short but very friendly. This was the first time Pongou had met Simon since taking office as Prime Minister. At half past twelve in the afternoon, Simon took a plane back to London, will handle diplomatic affairs for two days, and then rushed to Geneva to attend the League of Nations Committee of Nineteen on Monday. (Eleventh Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Foreign Secretary Simon has recovered from his convalescence in Monte Carlo in the Mediterranean and will depart from there tomorrow or Thursday to attend the League of Nations Committee of Nineteen to discuss the Manchurian problem. (Tenth Havas Dispatch)

Soviet Russia Upholds Peace and Never Forgets National Defense

Stalin Says Neglecting Heavy Industry Would Mean

Inability to Resist Strong Neighbors if They Invade

Japan Has No Intention of Concluding a Non-Aggression Pact with Russia

(Moscow) Stalin, as the Secretary-General of the Communist Party and the de facto head of the Soviet government, declared today that Soviet industrial output at the end of 1932 was 334 percent greater than before the war. Stalin refuted the criticism of Russia's industrial policy, saying that if Russia abandoned or delayed its current industrialization policy and produced more clothing and shoes, it would not be able to have a locomotive or automobile industry, and it would not have important steel and iron factories, and it would be in a position of being unable to defend against capitalist neighbors who have modern weapons. Its situation would be the same as that of China today. (Tenth Reuters Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Foreign Ministry officials said that the real reason why the Japanese military demanded a huge military budget for the next fiscal year in Stalin's speech to the Central Committee of the Communist Party was because the Soviet Union, on the one hand, asked Japan to conclude a non-aggression treaty, and on the other hand, prepared the national industry for war. Therefore, the possibility of concluding a non-aggression treaty with Russia today has finally disappeared. (Eleventh Dentus Dispatch)

Japan Expands Air Force

Military Plans to Build 300 Airfields

Training a Large Number of Pilots for Combat

▲China United News Tokyo Dispatch on the 11th Since the failure of the Pacific crossing in 1929, the Japan Aviation Association has become increasingly passive. Recently, it has been urged by the military to start activities again this spring. Its work is to expand the air force. At present, there are about 380 civilian pilots in Japan. Because the country needs too few, there are often those who have not flown for a year. In this way, what they have learned becomes useless. If a war breaks out, this air force reserve cannot be applied in time. The Japan Aviation Association has seen this and has prepared several new types of aircraft for the practice and use of unemployed pilots. In addition, it mobilized the national rural army and youth corps, and persuaded local wealthy people to donate airfields. The youth corps and rural army must build airfields with obligation. The country will build up to 300 airfields. It is heard that there are already a dozen or so places where construction has begun. Hundreds of airfields will soon be realized in various parts of Japan.

Mexican People

Raid Japanese Embassy

▲China United News Tokyo Dispatch on the 11th According to a report received by the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs from the Japanese Embassy in Mexico, on the morning of the 9th, about 60 Mexican people, chanting slogans such as "Down with Japan" and "Down with Aggressors" along the way, gathered in front of the Japanese Embassy. Some people gave speeches to the crowd, scolding the Japanese army for its unprovoked invasion of China and the seizure of Shanhaiguan by force. The crowd was extremely angry for a time, and then threw stones at the embassy and vandalized it. The windows and doors of the Japanese Embassy were completely destroyed. The Japanese embassy staff urgently notified the Mexican police, who sent a large number of police to suppress the situation, and the crowd dispersed.

German Newspaper "Vorwärts" Worries About the Far East Situation

If Japan's Militarism is Not Curtailed

World War II Will Break Out Soon

(Berlin) The famous socialist newspaper "Vorwärts" commented on the Far East situation today, saying that if Japan's militarism is not immediately curtailed by international action, then a new world war will arrive in an instant. There is no doubt about this. The passivity of the great powers will inevitably result in the collapse of the League of Nations. If the League of Nations does not force Japan to stop its hostile actions and respect international treaties, then the international community will have no right to exist. (Tenth Reuters Dispatch)

South American God of War Grins Grimly

Peru-Colombia Conflict on the Verge of Eruption

Bolivian-Paraguayan Troops Fight Fiercely in the Rain

Havas Dispatch from Buenos Aires on the 10th It is reported that Colombia and Peru are about to clash over the Leticia affair. Peru has instructed its Commander-in-Chief, Ramos, to notify the Colombian military commander that if Colombian troops advance towards Leticia, it will be a "casus belli." Colombian Commander General Copo replied that he did not know whether General Ramos represented the Peruvian rebels or the Peruvian government. He was ordered to command the troops to restore order within his own country, and his actions were in full compliance with the various treaties in force. Colombian troops have now set off towards Leticia and have arrived in the Manos region.

▲Reuters Dispatch from Buenos Aires on the 10th Although it is now the rainy season, the fierce battles between Bolivia and Paraguay in the Chaco forest have not diminished. There has been heavy rain recently, and the forest has become a swamp, but the two sides still confront each other. Although Paraguay's strength is far less than that of the enemy, it is costly for the enemy to gain an inch of land. The Bolivian army has suffered considerable losses, but it is still advancing fiercely. Today it won another victory and captured a fort. The Bolivian army has now penetrated deep into the forest, less than one hundred and seventy-five miles from the Paraguayan capital.

The Situation in Spain Becomes Increasingly Serious

Valencia Organizes Soviet Government

General Strike Declared in Seville and Other Places

Reuters Dispatch from Madrid on the 10th According to various sources, the spread of revolutionary forces within Catalonia is now causing great anxiety to the Spanish authorities. The serious state of affairs in the riots is the rebels' fierce attack on gunpowder bureaus and armories, the purpose of which is to increase the supply of armaments and ammunition. In two small towns in the province of Valencia, farmers have declared a Soviet Republic. The army suppressed them today, killing four people.

▲National Dispatch from Madrid on the 10th Today, the Seville local union declared a general strike, and the situation is serious. Police clashed with strikers, killing two policemen and wounding four strikers. The police arrested several people and seized a large number of arms.

▲National Dispatch from Madrid on the 11th After the general strike in Seville, it has now spread to the ports of Valencia and Cadiz, and workers in both ports have also had several clashes with the police. There was a bomb explosion in the port of Grao de Castellón, killing three people. In addition, militants attempted to stop trams and fired at security teams. There was also a shooting incident in Seville last night. The number of militants arrested has reached two hundred and eighty. The Spanish government is now planning to ask Congress to quickly pass a bill to hand over all those arrested to military tribunals for trial. This move is actually equivalent to declaring martial law, but although the situation is serious, the government does not want to declare martial law at present, but is determined to do its best to quell the disturbances.

French Cabinet Passes Financial Plan

Increasing Revenue and Reducing Expenditure to Balance the Budget

National Dispatch from Paris on the 10th French Finance Minister Cheron presented a method to balance the budget in the cabinet meeting today. According to Cheron's estimates, the current fiscal year will be short 10.4 billion francs. It is planned to save 5.3 billion francs by reducing government expenditure and raise 5.4 billion francs through increasing taxes and issuing bonds. The taxes to be increased include income tax, transfer tax, and sugar and coffee tax.

▲Havas Dispatch from Paris on the 11th The outline of the plan set by Finance Minister Cheron has been unanimously approved by the Cabinet, but the full text of the plan and its implementation will be finalized at the Council of State on Monday morning.

German Budget Deficit of 800 Million Marks

Reuters Dispatch from Berlin on the 10th The amount of the German budget deficit seems to be quite large. The Minister of Finance told the parliamentary budget committee today that it is estimated that the current fiscal year will be short about 800 million marks by the end of March. He also said that the previous budget was short 169 million marks and has not yet been made up. The funds saved in the current year may not be able to offset increased and unexpected expenditures. The country will encounter unarranged short-term debt of about 2.1 billion marks on April 1.

Germany Will Send Military Attachés to Major Cities Around the World

Result of Recognition of Military Equality

National Dispatch from Berlin on the 10th Previous reports that the German government will begin to send military attachés to foreign embassies have now been officially confirmed. It is reported that the letters of appointment will begin on April 1. Army attachés will first be stationed in London, Paris, Rome, Moscow, Prague, Washington, and Warsaw, and naval attachés will also be added to London, Paris, and Rome. These military attachés may also hold the position of military attaché in other neighboring countries in the future. Furthermore, these military attachés will be subordinate to the ambassador or minister, and their reports must be submitted to the ambassador or minister directly under their jurisdiction. This point is slightly different from before the European War. At that time, although the military attaché was an employee of the embassy, all reports were not submitted by the ambassador or minister. It is heard that the countries concerned have notified the German government and agreed to the dispatch of military attachés.

Trotsky Sick in a Foreign Land

Daughter Commits Suicide Due to Illness

Reuters Dispatch from Berlin on the 11th Trotsky's daughter, who is currently being treated for lung disease in Germany, died of gas poisoning today. According to a dispatch from Constantinople, Trotsky himself is also seriously ill in Prinkipo and has hired a specialist doctor from Geneva to visit him.

▲National Dispatch from Berlin on the 11th Madame Volron, daughter of the Communist leader Trotsky, suddenly committed suicide by opening a gas pipe in her apartment in the suburbs of Berlin. She was only thirty-two years old. Madame Volron had recently separated from her husband, Volron, and made a living by teaching. She left a letter to the landlady, saying that she was committing suicide due to multiple illnesses, and asked her to take good care of her young son. Madame had only obtained a temporary residence permit, which was about to expire, and she seemed to be deeply concerned about the possibility of being deported, and felt a sense of hopelessness, so she had the idea of giving up on life. Madame was the daughter of Trotsky's ex-wife. There is a half-brother studying in Germany, and the six-year-old child she left behind will be temporarily raised by her uncle.

London Fog

Trains Delayed, Ships Collide

London, 10th (Havas) - Dense fog has blanketed London and its suburbs. Buses are unable to operate, and many trains are delayed. While various vehicles in the city are moving extremely slowly, collisions are still unavoidable. Two steamships at sea also collided, fortunately without major damage.

Wireless Communication Between India and Japan

Bombay, 11th (Havas) - Sir George Ernest Schuster, Finance Member of the Viceroy's Executive Council, today held the opening ceremony for direct wireless telegraph communication between Bombay and Japan. Schuster sent a congratulatory telegram to Japanese Minister of Communications, Hiroshi Minami. A banquet was held afterwards, during which the Governor-General of India, Lord Willingdon, sent a telegram to the wireless telegraph company, expressing his hope that international friendship would be further enhanced by this new method of communication.

Key Points of the Regulations for Aviation and Highway Construction Lottery

Issued Four Times Annually with a Committee Established

Prizes Paid in Full Without Discounts

(Nanjing) The key points of the National Government's Aviation and Highway Construction Lottery Regulations, passed by the Central Political Council on the 11th, are as follows: (1) Unregistered lottery tickets will be issued four times a year, with 500,000 tickets each time, priced at ten national currency units per ticket. (2) The National Government will establish a special Aviation and Highway Construction Lottery Committee, inviting prominent figures from the Chinese and foreign financial, commercial, and industrial sectors, and designating representatives from the Control Yuan, the Directorate-General of Budgets, Accounts and Statistics, and the Ministry of Finance, to serve as members. The Minister of Finance will serve as the ex-officio chairman, responsible for supervising all matters related to the issuance of lottery tickets and managing the income from ticket sales. (3) The National Government will establish an Aviation and Highway Construction Lottery Office to handle issuance matters. (4) Fifty percent of the ticket revenue will be used for expenses related to issuance, office operations, and sales commissions, and the remainder will be used to fund aviation and highway construction. The remaining fifty percent will be used as prize money, with the following distribution: one first prize ticket, worth 500,000 yuan in silver; two second prize tickets, worth 100,000 yuan in silver each; four third prize tickets, worth 50,000 yuan in silver each; ten fourth prize tickets, worth 10,000 yuan in silver each, totaling 100,000 yuan in silver; fifty fifth prize tickets, worth 2,000 yuan in silver each; one hundred sixth prize tickets, worth 500 yuan in silver each; five hundred seventh prize tickets, worth 200 yuan in silver each; 4,999 tickets with the same last two digits as the first prize, worth 7 yuan in silver each; 44,999 tickets with the same last digit as the first prize, worth 20 yuan in silver each. (5) Lottery prizes will be paid in full without discounts. (6) Any remaining unsold lottery tickets from each issuance will be recognized by the Ministry of Finance, and the prize money will be paid in full according to the aforementioned prize amounts, regardless of the number of tickets actually sold. (7) The lottery drawing will be held publicly in Shanghai each time, with representatives from the Lottery Committee, the local court, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and the Shanghai Banking Association present to supervise. (11th Special Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Explains the Time Limit for Reporting Disasters

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has explained the time limit for reporting disasters. Flood disasters must be surveyed and reported one day before the beginning of autumn. Autumn disasters must be surveyed and reported one day before the beginning of winter. Drought and insect disasters must be surveyed and reported by the county magistrate at any time. Wind and hail disasters must be surveyed and reported no later than three days. The Ministry of Finance has also consulted with the Ministry of Interior to seek its opinion. (11th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Soldiers Conduct Inspection in Hankou

Sakano Also Goes to the Upper Reaches for Inspection

Our Navy Also Heavily Redeploys

Hankou Correspondence: Since the September 18th Incident, Japan has used the pretext of protecting overseas Chinese and has stationed a large number of warships in Hankou. The situation became even more serious after the Shanghai war. After the ceasefire, it gradually calmed down. Recently, Japanese troops suddenly occupied Yuguan, and the situation in North China is urgent. The Yangtze River region will inevitably have demonstrations again. Five Japanese warships, Ataka, Hira, Tsushima, Atami, and Kotaka, which were originally docked in Hankou, opened another Uji on the 8th. They are all docked on the Jiangmian River in the Japanese Concession, connected from end to end. The highest military officer is Sakano, commander of the 1st Foreign Dispatch Fleet. On the 6th, he led 24 platoons of marines to land for tactical exercises, firing live ammunition. It lasted a long time. At 11:00 AM on the 9th, he also inspected the marines of the six ships, Uji, Tsushima, Hira, Atami, Ataka, and Kotaka, and more than 1,000 marines stationed in Hankou on Kawamura Street in the Japanese Concession. After Sakano finished speaking and inspecting, he went to the banquet of Japanese overseas Chinese. It was decided that at 8:00 AM on the 10th, he would take the Atami warship to the west to inspect the Japanese warships in the upper reaches, and the Hira would follow him. It is scheduled to arrive in Yichang on the 15th, head east on the 18th, and return to Hankou on the 20th. Wang Shoutin, commander of the Chinese Navy's torpedo fleet stationed in Hankou, said that because diplomacy is strained and Japanese warships are being transferred frequently, he has redeployed the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. From Yichang to Wuxue, a total of more than 20 warships, including Minquan, Chu Tai, Jiang Kun, Chu Tong, Chu You, Chu Qian, Wei Sheng, Jiang Xi, Shun Sheng, Cheng Sheng, De Sheng, Ren Sheng, Yi Sheng, and Chen-class torpedo boats and Su-class torpedo boats, are stationed there, and the river defense is extremely solid. (January 9)

He Jian's Grief and Indignation at the Fall of Yuguan

Telegraphs Zhang Xueliang to Supervise the Troops and Kill the Enemy

Urges Sichuan and Guizhou Generals to Stop Fighting and Resist Aggression

Changsha Correspondence: After the news of the fall of Yuguan reached Hunan, the people of the three Hunan regions were extremely indignant. Various groups of farmers, businesses, industries, students, and women in the province and city scheduled to hold an emergency joint meeting at the Sun Yat-sen Hall on the 7th to discuss countermeasures. It is said that three proposals have been predetermined: (1) Eliminate all enemy goods in Changsha City. From now on, anyone found smuggling enemy goods will be executed. (2) Petition the provincial government to forward a telegram to the central government, clearly ordering the deployment of troops from all over the country to fight. (3) Telegraph all military personnel and people's groups across the country to inspire great conscience and rise up to save the country. Furthermore, the entire committee of the Changsha Municipal Party Headquarters, including Liu Wonan, issued a public telegram on the 6th, saying that because the violent Japan is wreaking havoc, the party has no way to save the country from danger, so it has voluntarily requested to be relieved of their duties to avoid occupying positions and being ridiculed. This also shows their grief and indignation. He Jian, chairman of the provincial government, also sent two telegrams, one asking Zhang Xueliang not to hesitate to sacrifice himself and supervise the troops to kill the enemy, and the other asking the generals of Sichuan and Guizhou to stop fighting and resist aggression. The telegrams are as follows:

(To Zhang Xueliang in Beiping) Director Zhang Han'gong, I was shocked and saddened to hear the news of the loss of Yuguan. The Japanese wolf has a vicious ambition to annex North China, and you are in charge of the key to the eastern gate. How could you not hear the news of the war and give such an important place to the enemy? I urge you not to hesitate to sacrifice yourself, supervise the troops and kill the enemy, have the determination to save the city, and come up with a plan to sink the boat and break the cauldron. Every inch of land is precious, and your reputation will be even greater. I am not talented, but I vow to lead the people of the three Xiang regions, sleep on our weapons and be vigilant, and provide you with support. Looking north at the smoke and dust, my heart aches. Please understand my stupid words and give me your kind words. He Jian kowtows and sings.

(To the generals of Sichuan and Guizhou) Sichuan Chairman Liu Zigan, Director Liu Fu Cheng, Guizhou Commander Mao Qunlin, Chairman You Yongnong, and Army Commander Wang Shaowu, I was shocked and saddened to hear the news of the loss of Yuguan. The gate has been opened, and Pingjin is shaking. The fate of the country and the nation depends on a moment. If we can unite to resist aggression at this time, there may be something we can do. If disaster is imminent, and the wall has not been removed, let me ask, if the country is no longer a country, what else is there? All of you have shown your loyalty and righteousness, and the world admires you. I know you must feel the same grief and indignation when you hear this bad news. I hope you will resolve all misunderstandings and stop the fighting immediately. Put the rights and wrongs to a public discussion, and go one step further, using the remaining bravery to attack the enemy. Achieve a deep friendship like Geng and Lin, and save the Zhao kingdom. I am incompetent, but I vow to lead the people of the three Xiang regions, walk in the dust, and fight against the violent Japan. With tears in my eyes, I submit my words. Please give me your instructions. Younger brother He Jian kowtows and sings. (January 7)
