Negotiation Progress Regarding the Matsui Incident

Matsui Leads Mongol Bandits to Attack Kailu

Captured Prisoner Confesses to Being Shot Dead in the Chaotic Army

Hashimoto Sends Telegram to Thank for Collecting Ashes

Shenyang Dispatch: Japanese militarists instigate the independence of Inner Mongolia, intending to unite Inner and Outer Mongolia and organize a so-called puppet Great Yuan State. The conspiracy documents have been revealed in newspapers. Now, we continue to find the documents of Yongatsu, the military attaché of the Japanese Army Representative Embassy in Beiping, negotiating with our Rehe authorities after the main culprit of the case, Colonel Kiyosuke Matsui, was killed. These documents are of utmost importance, so we will disclose them in their original form as follows: (1) On March 2nd, the Rehe military authorities received a letter from Yongatsu, the military attaché of the Japanese Army Representative Embassy in Beiping, forwarded by Huang Jinbiao, the director of the Beiping office, stating that Cui Xinwu, the brigade commander of the Ninth Cavalry Brigade of Rehe, and the special detachment, broke the agreement with Captain Hayama of the Japanese army stationed in Tongliao, and attacked the Mongolian Autonomous Army in the northeast of Kailu on February 25th, cruelly executing Kiyosuke Matsui, a Japanese army colonel who was the instructor of the army. The Japanese military headquarters expressed extreme regret for this action by the Rehe army. It was found that the Mongolian Autonomous Army still did not attack the Rehe army, and only acted in the Mongolian area north of the Xilamulun River (excluding Kailu and Linxi counties). Regarding this case, the Japanese military headquarters hopes to show sincerity, discuss solutions, and quickly reply to the representative military attaché Yongatsu, etc.

(2) On March 5th, the Rehe Army Headquarters telegraphed Huang, the director of the Beiping office, instructing him to go to the Japanese Embassy and question Military Attaché Yongatsu about where Matsui was killed and under what circumstances, urging him to reply quickly and report the negotiation situation at any time.

(3) On March 7th, Huang Jinbiao, the director of the Rehe Army in Beiping, reported the negotiation situation to the Rehe Army Headquarters as follows: (1) According to Yongatsu, Hayama, the commander of the Japanese garrison in Tongliao, wanted to allow the Mongolian army to pass through the border area of Kailu and Linxi, and invited Colonel Matsui to go with him. Biao immediately asked what the purpose of passing through Kailu and Linxi was. Yongatsu replied that it was a security operation, and said that Japanese Captain Hayama had already negotiated the passage with Brigade Commander Cui stationed in Kailu. Biao then questioned Yongatsu whether there were supporting documents or only verbal conversations. Yongatsu replied that he did not know. Yongatsu continued that when the Mongolian army arrived near Kailu, Brigade Commander Cui suddenly attacked the Mongolian army about twenty miles northeast of Kailu and killed Colonel Matsui. Biao immediately refuted Yongatsu, stating that the Mongolian army was not a formal army, but bandits disturbing local security, and that Colonel Matsui would not participate in such inferior bandits. Chairman Bi of the Rehe Army has not received a report from Brigade Commander Cui, and the truth will be discussed again. Yongatsu stated that as long as the Chinese side apologizes, the matter can be concluded and should not be delayed to avoid accidents. Biao stated that since the truth is not clear, there is no need or possibility to apologize. (2) Yongatsu also stated that he still intends to continue the previous discussions near Tongliao and proceed to the border near Kailu and Linxi. (4) On March 16th, the Rehe Army Headquarters telegraphed Brigade Commander Cui, asking whether there was a formal written contract for the operation of killing the Mongolian instructor Matsui. Since there were thousands of Mongol bandits attacking at the same time, how many casualties were there? Was Matsui's body only shot, or were there other injuries? It should be properly preserved, and the relics should also be properly stored as a basis for future negotiations. You should quickly reply in detail by telegram, and then negotiate with the Japanese side less, and do not use formal documents to avoid leaving any excuse. (5) On March 18th, Brigade Commander Cui telegraphed the headquarters, stating that the Japanese Matsui led more than 2,000 Mongolian troops westward, and Li's regiment repelled them, killing Matsui and more than 60 Mongolian soldiers. The entire process of blocking the attack has been reported by telegram. The bodies of Matsui and the Mongolian soldiers have been cremated by the local people, but Matsui's body has been photographed, and its bones are now being preserved. The documents and evidence obtained were previously brought to Rehe by Li, the leader of the special detachment. The brigade commander has not yet negotiated with the other party.

(6) On April 4th, the Rehe Headquarters sent a letter to Military Attaché Yongatsu, stating that Rehe Province has been making every effort to protect officials and civilians of your country, and there has been no lack of care. Unexpectedly, on February 25th, Brigade Commander Cui killed Matsui among the Mongol bandits in the defense zone. Afterwards, it was learned that Matsui was among them. According to the captured Mongol bandit Chaggan Buhe, during the fierce battle, we had more than a hundred casualties, and the crowd retreated. Matsui ordered a counterattack, but the crowd did not listen. Matsui opened fire to stop them, which aroused public outrage. The crowd opened fire and shot randomly. At that time, Matsui was shot and fell to the ground, and everyone took the opportunity to disperse. I was injured in my right side and could not move, so I was brought here. The brigade commander originally knew Matsui in Linxi, and immediately ordered to search for him among the corpses of the Mongol bandits. His head was found to have a penetrating gunshot wound, and he had already died. Diaries and other items were also obtained. Fearing that the body would rot in the heat, a photo was taken first, and then, according to Japanese customs, it was cremated and the ashes were properly preserved for his family to retrieve in the future. It is thought that Mongol bandits commit all kinds of atrocities, invading Kailu and disturbing our defense zone. The brigade commander was ordered to defend the territory and had the special responsibility of suppressing bandits. Matsui was a Japanese colonel who commanded Mongol bandits, which is quite inappropriate. It should be requested that your department negotiate with the Japanese authorities based on reason, and that such incidents should not happen again. It is believed that Brigade Commander Cui's suppression of bandits in the province is purely legitimate defense. Matsui aided the Mongol bandits in disturbing our defense zone, which is deeply regrettable. As for his being shot and killed, it was his own fault, and the Chinese side is even more unable to take responsibility. Following the previous cause, the situation is truthfully reported, and I would like to ask your military attaché to convey our regards to the authorities for their consideration, and hope that you will prevent such incidents from happening again in the future, so as to strengthen our good relations.

(7) On June 5th, the Rehe Headquarters received a telegram from Shao Zifeng, a senator, stating that:

The other party firmly requests to transport Matsui's remains to Beipiao.

(8) On June 21st, the Rehe Headquarters telegraphed Senator Shao, stating that according to Brigade Commander Cui's telegram, the official sent the adjutant of this headquarters, Ju Bingjun, to escort Matsui's remains to Beipiao on the day of respect. The senator should follow this order.

(9) On July 4th, a telegram was received from Hashimoto, the chief of staff of the Japanese Kwantung Army, stating that Matsui's ashes were escorted to Beipiao by the noble commander's representative and handed over to our representative Ishimoto. Thank you very much for your kindness. (Shenshi News Agency)

The Northeast Problem and the League of Nations (10) (1)

Representative Gu's Righteous and Stern Words

Dr. Gu Weijun, the representative of our country, rose and said, "It is now late, and the points raised by the Japanese representative are numerous, and it may take me a long time to respond to each of them in detail. I respectfully ask the chairman to allow me to make a more detailed reply at the next meeting. However, regarding some of the Japanese representative's points, please allow me to briefly state the Chinese side's views at this time, which will take no more than ten to fifteen minutes. I hope the members of the Administrative Yuan will consider this. The opinions expressed by the Japanese representative are very detailed and comprehensive. Now, I will only briefly respond to two or three of them. First, the Japanese representative denied what I said yesterday about Japan's continental policy, and claimed that Japan loves peace and is the best in the world. They even said that what Japan gives is more than what Japan takes. Gentlemen, you must still remember what I said yesterday. At this time, I only need to mention a few place names to aid your memory, such as the Ryukyu Islands, Taiwan, Korea, Manchuria, Mongolia, and now Rehe, etc. The Japanese representative also mentioned these territories. Who currently occupies them? The Japanese representative also tried hard to argue that the so-called Tanaka Memorial was forged, and made statements about Prime Minister Tanaka's itinerary, the biography of Director Fukushima's eldest daughter, and her age. However, regardless of whether the memorial is genuine or forged, the most important part of it was not mentioned by the Japanese representative. What is this most important part? It is the point about the necessity of Japan occupying Manchuria or Mongolia to create a leading position in North China and East Asia. For the past few decades, Japanese policy has been based on this backbone, but the Japanese representative denied that the so-called Tanaka's active policy was created and developed by the Tanaka Memorial. Page 41 of the Investigation Committee's report states, "The Tanaka Cabinet's active policy attaches great importance to the necessity of not treating Manchuria and other parts of China in the same way." From this, we can know the reason for the current situation in the three eastern provinces and Japan's efforts to isolate the three eastern provinces from the Chinese mainland. The report also states, "Japan has frankly stated that if turmoil affects Manchuria and Mongolia, affecting its security and endangering our special position and interests in the region (the above text is the same as that used in the Tanaka Memorial), Japan will rise up to protect it, regardless of where the threat originates." The Investigation Committee also expressed its opinion, "The Tanaka policy clearly states that Japan is responsible for maintaining security in Manchuria, which is different from the previous policy that only aimed to protect Japanese interests." We should also remember that Prime Minister Tanaka was the one who sent troops to China in 1927 and 1928 to hinder the work of the victorious army of the National Revolution to unify China. The facts that are revealed to us are much more powerful than verbal arguments, and I don't need to repeat them. I would also like to tell the members of the Administrative Yuan that even if the Tanaka Memorial is indeed forged, it must be a masterpiece by the Japanese. Chinese people will never be able to see the policies that modern Japan has enshrined as the norm in such a broad, comprehensive, detailed way. From China's position, it is convinced of the reasons for the authenticity of this memorial. Since 1905, for 27 years, Japan has repeatedly stated that China had made an agreement allowing Japan not to build a railway line parallel to the South Manchuria Railway. This year, Japan still has a semi-official document issued from Tokyo, stating that China and Japan have concluded 16 secret treaties, while the Chinese side completely denies this matter. So, does this secret treaty really exist? China has never recognized this agreement, but as far as I know, Japan notified European and American countries a few years ago, claiming that Japan opposes China's railway construction plan in the three eastern provinces, and that British, American and other countries' banking groups must not implement this plan, because China has this treaty obligation to fulfill. Regarding this point, we can find out the truth by looking at the words of the Investigation Committee. The report says, "We can now declare that the so-called promise of the Chinese plenipotentiaries attending the Beijing Conference between November and December 1905 regarding the parallel railway is not recorded in any formal treaty. However, this so-called promise is recorded in the minutes of the 11th day of the Beijing Conference on November 4, 1905. We have also obtained the agreement of the Japanese and Chinese representatives participating in this investigation team to acknowledge that there are no other documents containing this promise other than what is recorded in the Beijing Conference minutes." The above is just one point. Now, please allow me to present another point for you. Members of the Administrative Yuan, do you still remember when Japan suddenly submitted the Twenty-One Demands to the Chinese government in 1915 like a bolt from the blue? When European and American countries heard about it, they formally raised questions, but the Japanese government denied it, arguing that the Twenty-One Demands were non-existent and were completely alarmist words from China. Later, the governments of European and American countries received the full text of the Twenty-One Demands and inquired in Tokyo again, but Japan still firmly denied it. Japan made threats to China when submitting the Twenty-One Demands, demanding strict confidentiality and not leaking them to other countries, otherwise all consequences would be borne by the Chinese government. However, the European and American countries did not know how they obtained the full text of the Twenty-One Demands. Imagine what the Japanese diplomatic representatives in Europe and America would do at that time? They had no choice but to ask Tokyo for instructions. When the instructions arrived two or three days later, they claimed that only 11 of the so-called Twenty-One Demands were actually demands, and the remaining articles were only what the Japanese government hoped the Chinese government would consider. However, upon closer inspection of their content, they were actually of a demanding nature. After the Chinese government's experience with the above, once it sees the contents of the Tanaka Memorial, whether it is genuine or forged, how can it not feel extremely uneasy? I only have one comment on this, that is, what Japan did a few years ago is no different from what it is doing today. There is another point in the Japanese representative's statement that he hopes to convince me, that is, his so-called economic severance is a disguised form of war. The Japanese representative claimed that economic severance is as evil as war, or even worse than war. The Japanese representative is referring to the three eastern provinces. However, in China's view, since the three eastern provinces have been forcibly occupied by Japan and separated from China, economic severance is undoubtedly a peaceful self-defense strategy. Mr. Matsuoka gave a long description of the so-called Chinese xenophobia and its terrible consequences, and claimed that 15 million Chinese youths will not know where they are going in the future, and the threat to the world will be enormous. I have already explained to you yesterday that China does not have xenophobic ideas, and there is no need to repeat it here. Please refer to what I said yesterday. As for the request that the League of Nations Administrative Council find a way to solve this problem, we believe that after the Japanese army withdraws from the three eastern provinces and the threat to peace in the Far East is eliminated, the League of Nations will still have plenty of time to discuss it. Mr. Matsuoka also made statements about the current situation in China, and mentioned the Sino-Russian Treaty of 1898. The conclusion of this treaty was after the Sino-Japanese War, the Sino-Japanese War was the Korean War, which was created by Mutsu Munemitsu at the most opportune time. Mutsu issued an order to the Japanese envoy stationed in Seoul, saying, "Do not hesitate to use any excuse to take active action." You should still remember that what China hoped to be forcibly taken away by Japan could still be returned to China, so it concluded the Sino-Russian Treaty with Russia. Mr. Matsuoka expressed his displeasure with the joint intervention of Russia, Germany, and France against Japan. In fact, from our perspective, this matter is very reasonable. If the three countries could still help us with the three eastern provinces, then the three eastern provinces would still be Chinese territory, and there would be no Manchurian problem today. The Japanese representative also raised a point, hoping to convince the members of the Administrative Yuan, that is, Japan sincerely wants to help the Chinese people, and Japan sincerely wants to see China's unification. However, Japan's plan to help China's unification is the military action in Shanghai, the bombing of unarmed towns, and the occupation of Chinese territory that is wider than Germany and France. Even today, the Japanese army is still fighting against the Chinese people who oppose the puppet organization. If this is to help China's unification, then I would like to say to the Japanese representative, China does not welcome Japan's help. We cannot achieve the union of a family by robbing one of its members. We cannot achieve the unification of China by separating the most fertile part of China's territory. In other words, the picture drawn by the Japanese representative is very different from the facts. What are the facts? The Investigation Committee's report has them all, and there is no need to repeat them. As for other important issues, it is too late now, and I will present them to you at the next meeting." Liu Xiang Expresses His Determination to Fundamentally Eliminate Liu Wenhui

After the Neijiang Conference, Three Routes Attack Jiaren

Daily Military Expenditure Exceeds 300,000 Yuan

Looting Exceeds 100 Million Since the Outbreak of War

Inducing Guizhou Troops into Sichuan to Expand the War

Chongqing Dispatch: After Liu Xiang, Yang Sen, and others held a meeting in Neijiang, which closed without satisfactory results, the depressed Sichuan situation has become tense again. On the 6th, Liu Xiang mobilized the entire army from Zigong, dividing it into three routes to advance on Liu Wenhui's army. The first route was the First Division, led by Division Commander Tang Shizun, leading ten regiments to attack Meishan. The second route was the Fourth Division, led by Division Commander Fan Shaozeng, leading twelve regiments to cross the river from Weiyuan and attack Jiading. The third route was the Teaching Division, led by Division Commander Pan Wenhua, leading ten regiments to attack Jingyan. The Second Division, led by Division Commander Wang Zanxu, was in the middle to respond, with a force of thirteen regiments. Liu Xiang led fifteen regiments of troops to oversee the battle. In the Renshou area, Li Qixiang and Luo Zezhou's troops were responsible. The attack was launched on the morning of the 7th. The Chongqing army, both land and air, advanced together, and fierce battles took place in Mataping, Jingyan, and Qianfosi in Jiading. Liu Xiang's planes fiercely dropped bombs on the positions, killing many soldiers of Liu Wenhui's army and civilians in the war zone. The deaths on both sides were more than 3,000, and the front lines have not changed. Liu Xiang also urgently transferred the machine gun four regiment, two artillery regiments, and four planes from the rear to the front lines to launch a full-scale attack. According to Liu Xiang, he will not stop fighting until Liu Wenhui's army is fundamentally eliminated, and he said that there is no hope of unifying the Sichuan situation without completely resolving Liu Wenhui. He also declared to his troops that as long as the 24th Army is defeated, the 21st Army can dominate Sichuan. The armies were convinced without being intimidated. After unifying Sichuan, they will invade Guizhou, and all the generals have high hopes. Therefore, all the generals are willing to die for him. Liu Xiang also rewarded the soldiers with heavy money to encourage morale. However, the war has been prolonged and unresolved, and the army's finances are very alarming. The grain taxes in various counties in the garrison area have been collected until the 51st year of the Republic of China. Temporary military expenses have been levied five or six times. In addition, the market is sluggish, business is not prosperous, and tax revenue has decreased, making it more difficult to support the war. A day of combat costs 300,000 yuan. Liu Xiang has no way to cope, and is now issuing grain credit tax coupons on a large scale, forcing them to circulate in the market. They have been issued thirteen times, each time for 3 million, totaling 39 million. There are no reserve funds, and the situation is precarious. The Chongqing banks that Liu Xiang has forced to borrow from include Ju Xingcheng Bank for 1 million, Chuan Kang Zhili Bank for 500,000, Bank of China for 2 million, Meifeng Bank for 1 million, Pingmin Bank for 500,000, Shimin Bank for 500,000, Yanyue Bank for 1 million, and Commercial Bank for 500,000, totaling more than 7 million. Other money shops and large merchants have also borrowed money. The total amount of debt owed by Liu Xiang's army is now more than 80 million, plus the grain credit tax coupons issued without funds, totaling more than 110 million. Each day the war is prolonged, Liu Xiang's army owes 300,000 more in debt. Therefore, Liu Xiang is eager to resolve the war. However, the allied forces have undergone changes. Yang Sen, Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, and others are dissatisfied because Liu Xiang controls the counties in the defense area obtained from Liu Wenhui's army and monopolizes the salt funds from Zigong. They are unwilling to attack Liu Wenhui's army again. Liu Wenhui calmly dealt with Liu Xiang, defended the Tonghe Minjiang area, deployed heavy troops, and built solid fortifications as a long-term plan. The Chongqing army could not advance, resulting in the prolongation of the war. Therefore, Liu Xiang had to change his plan and sent a representative Lin to Kunming, Yunnan, to invite Guizhou troops to send troops, promising them common benefits, and helping Mao Guangyi to settle the Guizhou situation and resolve Wang Jialie, prompting Mao to send troops to help attack Liu Wenhui. According to Lin's telegram from Kunming, Long Yun has agreed and decided to send troops to help. In recent days, Guizhou troops have been found in the Huili area of southern Sichuan, totaling three regiments. However, they are stationed in Huili and have not yet advanced. Liu Wenhui telegraphed Guangdong, requesting them to stop the Guizhou troops from entering Sichuan, otherwise there would be no day of destruction. At the same time, he telegraphed Long Yun, inquiring about the truth of sending troops into Sichuan, and asked Long to clearly express his attitude. Long has not yet replied by telegram. As for the Guizhou army, now that the Guizhou situation has been roughly stabilized, the troops of Hou Zhidan, the commander of the Fourth Division, have surrounded Liu Wenhui's army in Jiading from the seven counties of southern Sichuan. It is reported that the battle is quite fierce. Mao Guangyi sent Jiang Zaizhen to lead four regiments into Sichuan to help Liu Xiang, hoping that Liu would help him settle the Guizhou situation. However, the 70 million people in Sichuan are still trying to stop the Sichuan military civil war, while Guizhou and Guizhou have entered Sichuan again, fueling internal strife, and the people will suffer even more. They unanimously telegraphed their resistance and asked the central government to seriously stop it, but the effect is not easy to judge. (8th)

The Qiongya Communist Bandits Will Be Eliminated

The Defense Army Uses the Miao People as Guides

Bandit Leader Wang Wenyu Has Been Captured Alive

Guangzhou Dispatch: Since Chen Jitang sent troops to recover Qiongya, he also abolished the Qiongya Special Zone. Chen Zhangfu was appointed as the director of the Qiongya Pacification Office, and the pacification work began. The suppression of the Communists is also progressing steadily. Qiongya has always been far from the provincial capital and close to the sea, and the Communist bandits have been using it as a nest for a long time. In recent years, the bandit forces have been quite large, and the pseudo-army has expanded to more than ten regiments, with Wang Wenyu, the pseudo-independent second division commander, in charge of everything. As a result, the trails of bandits are all over Qiongya. Recently, the Guard Brigade of the Defense Army has been specifically responsible for the search and suppression, and the bandit army has suffered casualties of seventy-eight percent. Only the bandit leader Wang Wenyu escaped into the mountains. In order to thoroughly eliminate the people, the Guard Brigade used the Miao people as guides and sent troops deep into the mountains to search. On the 2nd of this month, they captured the remaining fleeing bandits in Dajiliaoshan in the southeast of Yangjiang, Lehui County. The bandit leader Wang Wenyu was also arrested. Chen Hanguang, the brigade commander of the Guard Brigade, telegraphed from Yangjiang on the 3rd, reporting urgently that Wang Wenyu, the pseudo-division commander of the Communist bandits, was captured alive by the officers of this brigade in the forest of Dajiliaoshan in the southeast of Yangjiang, Lehui County, at noon on the 2nd. A pistol, forty bullets, a jade seal with the inscription "Headquarters of the Second Independent Division of the Pseudo-Chinese Red Army", a private seal of Wang Wenyu, two watches, a compass, a map, 32 yuan of central banknotes, and a fountain pen were seized. There were no other bandits with him. According to Wang, the entire Red Army in Qiongya has been completely wiped out, and only a few bandit leaders, such as Feng Fuquan and Nai Zheng, remain. Wang was sent to the Haikou Pacification Office for processing on the morning of the 3rd. In the past few days, Mo Battalion of the First Regiment killed a pseudo-division armory director in Shigungshan, seizing a gun and 22 bullets. Tang Battalion killed several bandits and captured more than ten bandits. Guan Ruishan has ordered Liu and Peng's regiments and the Miao people's vanguard to suppress them day and night, killing eight bandits, capturing nine male and female bandits, and seizing a Guangdong-made 79 rifle. (January 6th)

Jiangsong Raises Funds to Dredge Huxi River

The river channel starting from the Qiaonan Pier of the road outside the West Gate of this city, named Hushi River, is recorded in the local chronicles. To the south, it stretches to the Guyang Bridge Zhanran Nunnery, and is the source of drinking water for nearby residents, and the source of irrigation for hundreds of acres of paddy fields in that area. Recently, it has not been dredged for a long time and has become silted up. Surprisingly, someone was measuring the river last night, which surprised the people who saw it. After inquiry, it was learned that Gu Jue, the director of the Shentian Bureau, intends to sell the river, and a certain Han is willing to pay to take over it. The news spread, and the farmers were panicked. They asked Sun Shaochi, the town mayor of the area, to find a way to stop it. Sun went to the bureau to inquire, but did not get any clear information. Therefore, the town mayor convened a meeting and decided to submit a request to the Finance Department to instruct the bureau to stop it, and to send a letter to the county bureau to stop the progress. At the same time, they will find ways to raise funds for dredging. The expenses have been enthusiastically acknowledged by the residents of the area, and the Construction Bureau is requested to send someone to survey it, so as to achieve the purpose of preservation.

Suzhou Suspected Murder Case Exhumed for Examination

Qian Yingen, a resident of Waikuatang Township, died after falling into the river last September. After the District Procuratorate completed its investigation, it decided not to prosecute. However, the deceased's family believed he had been beaten to death and appealed to the High Court for reconsideration. The High Court ordered the Wuxian District Procuratorate to exhume the body for a new examination. The court exhumed the body yesterday (the 10th) at an open space in Guanku Lane. After examination by the coroner and other officials, it was determined that there were no fatal injuries on the body. There was only a minor injury on the right hand, which was likely sustained when he fell into the river. The coroner immediately filled out the corpse identification form and awaited further investigation.

Anhui Refugees Disturb Suzhou Villages

A disturbance by refugees occurred in Guoxiang the day before yesterday, with daylight robbery of property and armed clashes with villagers. The situation has been calmed, and all the refugees have been sent out of the area. However, more than 200 Anhui refugees arrived in Xukou on the 10th. The local gentry and merchants provided them with travel expenses to leave. However, yesterday morning (the 11th), these refugees were discovered in Muduk Town, extorting goods from shops and homes. The town's public security authorities dispatched police to persuade them to temporarily stay in the City God Temple and await repatriation. The refugees were exceptionally unruly and refused to be suppressed, intending to cause trouble. The public security bureau telegraphed the county government, and a platoon of police was dispatched at noon to suppress them and prepare to send them out of the area.

Second Installment of Land Value Tax Levied

The Financial Bureau's assessment of the 21st year's land value tax for the autumn harvest has been approved by the provincial government, with a general reduction of 11.1%. After deducting wasteland exemptions, those who are behind on payments should receive a general reduction of 10.56%. Wasteland and arrears should be combined to reach 89% of the total. In addition to the full collection of the first 40%, the second 60% should be collected at 82.4% of the actual value, up to the Lunar New Year's Eve. Overdue payments will be subject to a late payment penalty of 10%. For every yuan of regular tax paid, an additional 1.2232 yuan will be collected for various expenses. The bureau notified all businesses yesterday (the 11th).

Wuxi Public Security Bureau Seizes Poison Pill Organization

The late Yang Yangwu of Tangtou Town, Sixth District, was a graduate of the National Chinese Studies Institute. After her husband's death, his wife, Wang, organized an operation to sell poison pills, wholesaling them to various towns. The business was thriving. The county public security bureau received a tip-off the day before yesterday and immediately dispatched a detective team with informants. They searched the premises and seized a large number of poison pills on the spot.

The witnesses were taken to the bureau for questioning.

Qianqiao Robbery Case Cracked in Changzhou

Robberies have occurred repeatedly in the Qianqiao area, under the jurisdiction of the First Police Station of the Ninth Branch Bureau in the Fourth District. Residents have been unable to sleep peacefully. The head of the Ninth Branch Bureau, Liu Chunlan, received a tip-off the day before yesterday that a suspect, Wang Guilin, was hiding somewhere. After receiving the tip-off, Director Liu went to the address and arrested Wang. Wang confessed that there were robbers hiding in Luoshe and a certain fish market in Changzhou. After obtaining the confession, Director Liu, accompanied by Inspector Zhu Wenyin and chief police officer of the branch office, went to Changzhou to search and arrest them. They successfully captured robbers Yao Meibao, Yao Meilin, and Wu Genying. The other 20 or so robbers had already fled upon hearing the news. Later, the Luoshe Chamber of Commerce captured a key suspect, Ding Dagou. The bureau escorted them to the case and awaited transfer to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Changzhou County Magistrate Zhang Interrogates Notorious Bandit

The Wuyi Detective Team previously captured the notorious bandit Shang Dianyuan in Shanghai. After being escorted to Changzhou, he was interrogated by Secretary Wu Jun of the county government and then sent to prison. Soon after, Secretary Wu received threatening letters from Shang's gang. A few days later, a robbery occurred at the home of Zhao Songping. County Magistrate Zhang investigated and found that the bandit had committed multiple robberies and other serious crimes in the past. The executed bandit Yu Chunyuan and others had confessed that Shang was the mastermind. The magistrate suspected that the bandit was involved in the robbery of the Zhao family, so he personally interrogated the suspect yesterday. Shang's testimony remained evasive. County Magistrate Zhang explained the principles of righteousness, then ordered him to be returned to prison and await further investigation.

Zhenjiang Provincial Government Allocates Funds to Build Sluice Gates

The Jiangsu Provincial Government believes that the Wang and Zhu Rivers are deeply connected to the water conservancy of the counties downstream of the Jiangbei region. Last year, the Labor Relief Bureau used labor-for-relief methods to straighten the two rivers. If sluice gates are not built in time to control the water flow, it will cause significant harm. Local organizations have repeatedly requested that funds be allocated for the construction of these gates. The provincial government believes that this should be approved immediately. Therefore, it ordered the Department of Construction to immediately withdraw 150,000 yuan in construction bonds from the road construction funds and hand them over to the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau for verification and reserve. Construction should begin immediately according to the original sluice gate construction plan.

Reduction in Wheat Cake Business Tax

The Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation believes that wheat cakes and bean cakes are essential items needed by farmers for agricultural production. In addition to fertilizing fields and feeding livestock, they are also necessities for poor people to make a living. The business tax should not be too high. They specially requested the Department of Finance to reduce or exempt the tax rate. Subsequently, the Department of Finance approved, stating that this year's low grain prices have harmed farmers, constituting a special circumstance that warrants appropriate relief. It approved a temporary collection of 2 per mille, according to the rice and flour industry tax rate, starting from the winter of the 21st year, to show compassion. The federation has already recorded the approval and sent letters to the various county chambers of commerce.

Nantong Strengthens Jianghai Port Defense

According to confidential reports received by the county magistrates and military and police authorities of Tong, Ru, Hai, and Qi, bandits are taking advantage of the situation to plan attacks. Defenses along the rivers and coasts of the Jianghai region have been strengthened. Emergency precautions are also being taken in the inland areas to prevent unexpected incidents.

Thorough Investigation of Liu Haisha's Opium Smuggling Case

The opium trade in Nantong is very active, and opium traffickers are very active. To avoid detection, they often wrap the opium in oiled cloth and throw it into the shallows, then retrieve it when the opportunity arises. Zhou Er, a resident of Liu Haisha Township, recently retrieved 16 pieces of opium from the Yangtze River at Shierxu Port and divided them with others. The Public Security Bureau investigated and arrested Zhou, sending him to the county for thorough investigation.

Danyang Zhang Guandu Robbery Injures Person

At 8 PM the night before last, eight or nine bandits armed with pistols and weapons suddenly broke into the shop of Zhang Chengrui, a businessman in Zhang Guandu, West Township, robbing more than ten yuan in cash. They then rushed into the house of Zhang Shucai across the street, looting extensively. As they left, they kidnapped Zhang's young son. The victim desperately chased after them and was shot and killed by the bandits. Afterwards, Zhang's family, Zhang Qishi, reported the incident to the county government. County Magistrate Wang specially dispatched Shen Cheng, accompanied by a coroner, to the township to investigate the scene.

Ningbo Yongchuan Ship Robbed in Shipu Waters

The Yongchuan ship of the Yongchuan Shipping Bureau on the north bank of Jiangbei, Ningbo, has been operating between Wenzhou and Ningbo for many years. At 5:00 PM on the 5th of this month, the ship departed from Ningbo for Wenzhou, carrying over 500 pieces of cargo and over 400 passengers. To prevent theft, the ship was equipped with five maritime police officers. At 6:00 AM on the 6th, the ship arrived at Shipu Wharf and unloaded cargo and passengers as usual. It then continued its journey. However, during the unloading of cargo and passengers, eight or nine Taiwanese bandits disguised as passengers boarded the ship. At about 7:00 AM, as the ship sailed through the Manshan waters, the bandits forced the ship to sail to Dasheng Island in Taizhou, more than 100 miles from Haimen. There, five more Taiwanese bandits boarded the ship and looted extensively. One water police officer, Jin Yun, two passengers, He Jinfa and Lian Gengsheng, three passengers, Xie Xinyuan, Xu Quanfa, and others, and the five Brownings and one wooden pistol carried by the maritime police team were all stolen by the bandits. Three young women among the passengers were raped and injured. In addition to the seven hundred yuan stolen from the purser's office, the clothing and silver of over 400 passengers were lost, estimated at over ten thousand yuan. After being robbed, the ship sailed from Haimen to Wenzhou on the evening of the 7th and should be returning today. After receiving a report from the Haimen branch bureau, the Ningbo bureau reported to the Maritime Police Bureau and relevant agencies, requesting investigation and pursuit.

News from the Jinjiang Fritillaria Sales Cooperative

Fritillaria is an important medicinal material, produced in the Zhangcun area of Yinjing Township, You County. Recently, the local farmers have realized that the quality of their products is declining and their livelihoods are difficult. To adapt to modern trends, they have initiated the organization of a cooperative to study cultivation and improve quality. All of the dried fritillaria produced next year will be centrally managed by the cooperative, which is automatically formed by the farmers. The sales volume will be limited, and sales will be made in batches. Based on social needs, an appropriate price will be set. It is heard that the planned sales volume is 500,000 catties per year, with a price starting at 100 yuan and increasing by 5 yuan each month, gradually increasing until supply and demand are balanced. Therefore, each household has decided to change from complex production to single production next spring. The various households have held many meetings and have submitted an application to the provincial and county governments for record, in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Industry and Rural Cooperatives.

Yangzhou County Magistrate Protects Mail Ships Along the Way

The Jiangsu Provincial Government approved a letter from the Jiangsu-Anhui Postal Administration stating that mail is transported by mail ships to and from various inland locations, which is very important to public transportation. However, recently, mail ships in the counties of Dongtai, Xinghua, Wujin, Taixian, and Liyang have been frequently robbed, which has greatly impacted the future of mail delivery. The county government was specially instructed to strictly prevent water bandits and to pay special attention to protecting mail ships along the way. After receiving the order, the county government has ordered the Public Security Bureau and police teams to comply.

Hangzhou Aviation School Training Plane Accident

A training plane from the Central Aviation School crashed about three miles from the school on the 10th, killing student Xie Zhongzhu and injuring instructor Li Junde. The accident occurred at 11:00 AM on the 10th. Li Junde, a major instructor in the aviation school's flight department, and student Xie Zhongzhu were flying together in a No. 3 training plane purchased from the United States. Li was piloting, and a foreign instructor and another student were flying in formation in a No. 12 training plane. In less than half an hour, the No. 3 plane, while practicing machine gun strafing from above, turned too quickly, causing the engine to stall. The nose of the plane pointed to the ground, the tail pointed to the sky, and it crashed to the ground. The fuselage was completely destroyed. Although the No. 3 plane was piloted by Li Junde, Xie Zhongzhu was sitting in front of Li Junde. After the plane crashed, Xie's head was fractured at the base of the skull. Li's left arm and right clavicle were broken, and he also suffered head injuries. Xie died half an hour after being injured. He was placed in a coffin at the hospital on the morning of the 11th, and the coffin was moved to Yangzhuang outside Qingbo Gate for temporary storage. A telegram was sent to Xie's family in Shantou, Guangdong, to come to Hangzhou to handle the arrangements. The deceased, Xie Zhongzhu, was from Dapu, Shantou, Guangdong, and was 22 years old. He was admitted to the aviation school in Beijing this time and had only been in school for three months. The injured Li Junde is from Liling County, Hunan, and is 25 years old. He graduated from the first class of the Central Military Academy's aviation program and has served as a pilot in the 4th Aviation Squadron. He came to the school last September to take on this position. Although his injuries are serious, his life is not in danger.

Xiaoshan Township Chief's House Burns Down

The home of Xia Qinglin, the township chief of Xiajia Township in the Fifth District of Xiaoshan, caught fire the night before last due to a cigarette butt burning the mosquito net. Fifteen buildings were destroyed, and all clothing and appliances were reduced to ashes. The loss is estimated at over 100,000 yuan.

Manager Dies by Suicide After Drinking

Hong Tianbao, the manager of Yishun Fruit Shop in Linpu Town, Xiaoshan, was fond of alcohol. On the night of the 6th, he drank too much and became mentally deranged. He went to the kitchen and committed suicide with a knife. By the time his colleagues found out, he was lying in a pool of blood and had died.

After the Resumption of Sino-Russian Relations, the Government Should Urgently Communicate Trade with Outer Mongolia

National Federation of Commerce Urges in Telegram Yesterday

丨 A Collection of Heavy Taxes Levied by the Kulun Government 丨

The National Federation of Commerce telegraphed the National Government Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Foreign Affairs and Industry yesterday. The telegram read: "To the National Government Executive Yuan, Ministries of Foreign Affairs and Industry: We have received a letter from Li 　shan, Ren Yuheng, Cui 　yu, Cheng Fan'an, Wang 　ting, etc., representatives of the merchants and people of Chahar Province, requesting an investigation.

Outer Mongolia is Originally Part of National Territory

It is an integral part of our country. Its vast area and abundant resources are almost the best among the provinces in the interior. In terms of politics, it can serve as our country's barrier. In terms of economy, it is enough to supply the people's livelihood. The people of Outer Mongolia are of the same nation as those in the country, and there is no separation in customs and habits. Moreover, there is a demand and supply relationship that cannot be separated. Therefore, there is a very long history of mutual benefit and coexistence. However, since the political reform of the Soviet Union, new trends have spread, and the thinking of the Mongolian people has changed. The young people are emotionally impulsive and easily agitated by the biases of socialism. Therefore, they changed their outward psychology and willingly accepted Soviet Russian protection. In the 13th year of the Republic of China, they organized a government in Ku Lun, intending to

Break Away from Our Country's Suzerain Relationship

From then on, the biggest change occurred in the political aspect between the interior of our country and Outer Mongolia. In terms of economy, trade between the interior and Outer Mongolia was also abruptly cut off. After the Sino-Russian negotiations on the Eastern Railway issue broke down, the weaker emotions of the Mongolian people showed further hatred for Chinese merchants. From then on, Chinese merchants in Ku Lun who were engaged in business and lived there were subjected to extremely harsh treatment. Not only was their property confiscated, and their human rights were trampled on, but they also had no freedom to enter, leave, or move, nor freedom to reside and do business. Hundreds of thousands of Chinese merchants in Ku Lun lived a miserable life, with each day feeling like a year. Their suffering and tragic situation are truly endless. Our government could not recover the lost Outer Mongolia, and it had no way to provide relief to the merchants living in Ku Lun, causing Zhangjiakou, which has the closest relationship with Outer Mongolia, to declare bankruptcy in all business matters. Now that

China and Russia Have Resumed Diplomatic Relations

We must quickly catch up and propose a rescue plan for negotiations with Russia. This is the first thing that should be carefully considered and planned. Furthermore, the commercial relationship between Zhangjiakou and Outer Mongolia has been at a standstill since the economic blockade of Outer Mongolia and the refusal of Chinese merchants to enter the country. The import of Mongolian goods has also stagnated at the same time. Both supply and demand have been greatly affected. The mutually beneficial relationship has turned into an antagonistic relationship for several years. However, after investigating the reasons, it is all because the emotions between China and Russia have not been reconciled, and the Mongolian people's perception of the interior is weak, leading them to express intimacy with Russia. This kind of fact can be stated by those familiar with the internal affairs of Outer Mongolia. Therefore, although the losses of Chinese merchants have reached 40 to 50 million yuan, the lack of material needs felt by the people of Outer Mongolia has also become a more serious situation. The key to this is whether China and Russia can understand each other. If China and Russia can truly restore friendly relations, our country's diplomatic authorities can naturally prescribe the right medicine and heal the gap between the interior and Outer Mongolia by

The Soviet Union is Responsible for Peaceful Resolution

Preserving the original friendly facts. The livelihood and national economy of the interior can obtain considerable gains. Outer Mongolia and the needs of a thriving population between China and Russia can also solve great difficulties. In a moment of transformation, several good things are achieved. This is the second thing that the government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs should set as a key condition for the first negotiations with Russia, to restore the mutually beneficial relationship between Zhangjiakou and the warehouse. Furthermore, our country's trade with Russia has always been backward. The goods that are shipped out are mainly soybeans from Manchuria, and the goods that are shipped out from Zhangjiakou are mostly silk and tea products, all of which are agricultural products. There are no industrial products for rotation. It is only used as raw materials for others, with no manufacturing capacity. In terms of capital, all are operated by private individuals with small capital, with no state-run or privately-run trading companies. Now, the economic policy of the Soviet Union is at its peak, and the five-year industrial plan is being implemented, with great results. With the capital of the country, it is confronting the capital of private individuals. Russian commerce will undoubtedly win. The development of our country's merchants' foreign trade may have no hope. Moreover, what we ship out are only a few kinds of raw materials, and what is rotated are mostly manufactured goods. The phenomenon of excess imports is unavoidable, and commercial competition is bound to fail. This is what should be paid attention to.

Now, we will take the

Two Key Points Within Our Limited Scope

First, the state should encourage the organization of jointly funded trading companies (such as exempting foreign trade goods from increased taxes, reducing freight, and protecting safety, stipulating laws, and providing special protection). Second, the state should promote jointly funded construction of the Zhang-Ku or Zhang-Duo railways, and develop the resources of Inner Mongolia, and open factories for various industries in Zhangjiakou (such as leather manufacturing, woodworking, ironware, and various manufacturing factories). Only in this way can there be a possibility of confrontation with Soviet Russian commerce. Otherwise, it will only be a slave market. This is the third thing that the government should implement commercial protection policies after Zhangku. Turning to the above two points, both are most closely related to our country's economy and the people's livelihood. They are the most important conditions in the Sino-Russian negotiations for the establishment of mutually beneficial trade treaties. The third opinion is an indispensable facility for developing the national and social economy and protecting the national economy and the people's livelihood. The representatives saw the lurking dangers ahead and asked your association to submit the information accordingly. On the one hand, the strategy for commercial relations between China, Russia, and Outer Mongolia should be carefully planned and secretly stipulated. On the other hand, the policy of protecting merchants should be determined and promulgated. If you do not abandon the humble opinions and adopt them, then the merchants in Russia and Mongolia will have a prosperous life. The reason for the electric presentation to your government and ministries is to ask you to examine and approve and implement them, so as to benefit trade, to the utmost degree. The attached documents are presented. Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, Lin Kanghou, bows, gray seal.

Yesterday Was Not a Shanghai-Beiping Flight Day

Heavy Wind and Snow Last Night

Difficult to Take Off This Morning

The Shanghai-Beiping route of China National Aviation Corporation has not taken off since it was blocked by heavy fog the day before yesterday. Because yesterday was not a flight day (the northbound days are Tuesday, Thursday, and Saturday), it still did not take off. The first flight will begin this morning. However, yesterday afternoon, the wind suddenly picked up, and snow fell in the evening. It is feared that it will not be able to take off again this morning. The westbound plane on the Shanghai-Hankou line was blocked by fog the day before yesterday and had to return four times. At 8:15 AM yesterday morning, pilot Gist still flew the No. 6 plane westward. The eastbound plane was blocked in Nanjing the day before yesterday, and it did not leave Beijing eastward until 7:50 AM yesterday morning, arriving in Shanghai at 9:50 AM. From this, it can be seen that the heavy fog the day before yesterday was only in the Beijing-Shanghai area. Yesterday, there was rain and no fog in Shanghai, and the plane could still take off. However, there was heavy fog above Hankou, causing the company's Chongqing-Hankou route, piloted by pilot Ge Fu in the No. 5 plane, to take off westward at 8:10 AM yesterday morning, but it had to return to Hankou at 9:40 AM.

Heavy Wind and Snow in Shanghai Last Night

Temperature Drops Suddenly

The weather in Shanghai has been changing erratically in recent days. The temperature changes suddenly. Although the sky was gloomy the day before yesterday, the temperature was quite high. There was no wind outdoors, and the thermometer rose to about 58 degrees. Even without wearing a fur coat, there was no cold feeling. By midnight, the weather suddenly changed, and the sound of rain continued all night. By yesterday morning, the temperature had dropped sharply, and the wind was very strong. Light rain was misty, and cold and dampness were combined. According to those who have lived in the north, this kind of weather sometimes occurs in late autumn and early winter. By about 9:00 PM, the wind was even stronger, snow fell from the sky, and the temperature also dropped, which was completely different from the day before yesterday.

Customs Ships to Adopt International Whistle Signals

One Short, One Long, and Two Short Sounds

Merchant Ships to Stop Immediately Upon Hearing This Signal

A special notice from the Jianghai Customs states: "By order of the government, the whistle signal previously used by customs ships—three short sounds followed by one long sound—to alert all sailing and steam vessels on the seas is hereby discontinued. Hereafter, customs ships will adopt the internationally recognized signal, consisting of one short sound, one long sound, and then two short sounds. This signal indicates 'stop ahead' and signifies that there is an important message to convey. All customs ships, regardless of the reason for requiring steam or sailing vessels to stop ahead, will use this signal. Please take note."

Dredging the River Channels in the Liuhuo Estuary War Zone

Yesterday's Meeting of the Four-County Committee

Resolved on Methods for Project Funding

Dong Xiujia, director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction, recognizing the importance of water conservancy in the province, specially established the Jiangsu Provincial Labor Conscription and River Dredging Committee. Because the river channels at the Liuhuo estuary have not been dredged for a long time, and have become even more silted up since the outbreak of hostilities on January 28, making navigation difficult, dredging is urgently needed. Zhu Kaiqiao and Cai Wangzhi were specially appointed as members of the Provincial Labor Conscription Committee and as the director and deputy director of the Liuhuo Branch, respectively. In addition, Wu Sheng-san, Zhu Menghao, Gu Jiqing, Pan Zhixing, Jin Jushan, Gu Zhenyi, and other local gentry from Taicang, Kunshan, Jiading, and Baoshan counties were appointed as members of the Liuhuo Branch. The county magistrates and construction bureau chiefs of the four counties of Taicang, Kunshan, Jiading, and Baoshan are ex officio members. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, Zhu Kaiqiao, the director of the committee, held the first committee meeting at 20 Renji Road in the Shanghai International Settlement. The county magistrates and construction bureau chiefs of the four counties, as well as the committee members, attended. Zhu Kaiqiao chaired the meeting. (1) Project Allocation: Resolved to allocate the project according to the existing plan of twelve shares: Kunshan's first project receives 2/12 shares, Taicang's second project receives 6.4/12 shares, Jiading's third project receives 2.4/12 shares, and Baoshan's fourth project receives 1.2/12 shares (However, the area of Baoshan that has been changed and incorporated into the city will be handled by the Department of Construction in consultation with the municipal government). (2) Project Funding Budget: Resolved to compile a detailed budget in accordance with the regulations of the Department of Construction for the meeting to decide. (3) Project Implementation Procedure: Resolved to build a dam on the 27th of this month, close the dam on February 6, release water on the 7th, hand over the river on the 17th, start digging on the 18th, and complete the work and open the dam on March 18. (4) Additional Committee Members: Resolved to recommend Jiang Hefang, Wang Zhenfei, Jin Boqin, and Hong Lanxiang as members and report them to the Department of Construction for additional appointment. (5) Mutual Election of Secretary and Economic Committee Members: Resolved to elect Wu Sheng-san as secretary and Jiang Hefang as economic committee member. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Pilots' Association Requests Registration

Shanghai dispatch from the Shishi News Agency: For decades, our country's piloting rights have been held by foreigners. Last year, our navigation industry strongly advocated for their recovery. The Ministry of Navy even established a pilot training school to nurture pilot talent and gradually prepare for their recovery. The Yangtze River, being our inland river, also employs foreign pilots due to treaty relations. Currently, there are 25 Europeans and Americans and 20 Japanese. Our national defense is entirely in the hands of foreigners. Therefore, our country's Yangtze River pilots have specially organized the Songhu Pilots' Association to petition the Ministry of Navy for registration and the issuance of a business license as a first step toward recovering Yangtze River piloting rights. Yesterday, they specifically notified all domestic pilots to register with the association and sent a letter to the Navigation Association stating that, starting in January of this year, all Chinese Yangtze River ships requiring pilots should only hire domestic pilots and should no longer use foreign personnel. They also reported to the central government, requesting that the number of foreign pilots be restricted and reduced annually, and that their terms of service be shortened.

Hydrographic Office to Measure Oriental Great Port on Behalf

Central News Agency reports: Regarding the matter of developing an Oriental Great Port, the Preparatory Committee for the Oriental Great Port has been conducting surveys of port sites separately and actively proceeding. Because the seabed depth changes rapidly, the committee has proposed conducting surveys once a year and has submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways to allocate funds for implementation. It is reported that the authorities of the Ministry of Finance, due to financial difficulties, are unable to allocate funds immediately. In order to implement the survey as soon as possible, they consulted with the Ministry of Navy and requested the Hydrographic Office to conduct the survey on their behalf every year. Therefore, the Hydrographic Office received Instruction No. 7835 from the Ministry of Navy the other day and immediately prepared a list of the required survey expenses for reporting. The original text of the joint consultation between the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways is recorded below: For the matter of consultation, it is based on the report from Chen , director of the Preparatory Committee for the Oriental Great Port: "We have examined the plan proposed by this committee for separately surveying port sites. In the plan, the marine survey should be conducted every March for four months, and preparations should be made to start the actual measurement at the end of this year. However, although this committee's budget has been ordered to be restored, it only covers surveys of water and landforms. Surveys of seabed depth are not included in the budget, and the steamships and instruments needed for marine surveys have not yet been purchased, and the cost of temporary expenses is also very large. Even if it can be received immediately, it will still take time to purchase and prepare. The proposed measurement plan cannot be realized immediately. In order to coordinate both considerations, we propose that your ministry consult with the Ministry of Navy and instruct the Hydrographic Office to survey the depth of the seabed of Donggang once every March for about four months, so as to avoid delays in the planned measures. In addition, we should submit the request to the Executive Yuan to approve the addition of 56,820 yuan in temporary expenses for this year, so as to purchase supplements and carry out the marine survey. Is it feasible? We should prepare a temporary expense budget and submit it for review and instructions, and implement it separately." Checking the survey of bays and seabed depths is indeed the work that the committee should prepare for, but central finances are difficult, and it is feared that the Ministry of Finance will not be able to allocate the 56,820 yuan of temporary expenses at one time. This ministry also feels economically exhausted and cannot afford to cover the full amount. In order to implement the survey of Donggang seabed depths as soon as possible, we should consult with your esteemed ministry accordingly and hope that you will check and inquire whether the Hydrographic Office can survey the depth of the seabed of the Oriental Great Port on your behalf every year, how much funding is required, and please instruct to reply immediately so as to handle it. As for inter-departmental friendship, Gu Shishi, head of the General Affairs Section of the Hydrographic Office, told a Central News Agency reporter that the work on the port site of the Oriental Great Port will take about two years to complete. The northern great port is currently unable to proceed due to the severe weather in the north, so it has been rescheduled to April.

Jiangwan Disaster Victims' Loan Measures

Statistics on 850 Extremely Poor Disaster-Stricken Households

Loan Value Vouchers Being Distributed Successively

After the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, acting on the order of the Municipal Government, coordinated with the Public Security and Public Works Bureaus to handle relief matters in the Jiangwan District, a decision was made after several investigations and consultations, and was submitted to the Municipal Government for approval. The bureau is now actively proceeding with it. A reporter from Riri News Agency learned about the progress of the handling as follows:

Screening Disaster Victims

Previously, the bureau and others reported that there were 1,015 poor people reported by the municipal commissioners who were in urgent need of relief. After the bureau and others sent personnel to conduct on-site inspections of each household separately, more than 100 households who had already started building houses or whose burned houses still had more than one room were removed. It was estimated that 850 households should be provided with relief, of which 202 households would be provided relief by the local maintenance association, and the remaining 648 households would be handled by the municipal government through fundraising.

Mapping Disaster Victims

After screening, the number of disaster victims mapped is as follows: 52 households in Jieshi No. 14, 46 households in Jieshi No. 92, 18 households in Tui No. 7, 44 households in Tui No. 8, 7 households in Yin No. 4, 6 houses in Yin No. 5, 19 households in Yin No. 6, 53 households in Yin No. 9, 22 households in Yin No. 10, 21 households in Yin No. 11, 6 households in Yin No. 76, 52 households in Yin No. 77, 105 households in Yu No. 15, 42 households in Yu No. 25, 38 households in Yu No. 29, 29 households in Guan No. 5, 37 households in Guan No. 16, 39 households in Guan No. 92, and 12 households in Jian No. 30. The above totals 648 households. The 202 households handled by the local maintenance association include 37 households in Jian No. 28, 68 households in Jian No. 32, 15 households in Jian No. 35, 21 households in Yu No. 26, and 51 households in Yu No. 34.

Fundraising Progress

For the 648 households handled by the municipal government, with a loan of 150 yuan per household, 97,200 yuan is required. In addition to the original 28,000 yuan allocated to the district for housing construction loans by the Shanghai War Zone Rehabilitation Committee, the remaining 69,200 yuan has been raised by the municipal government.

Loan Measures

It has been decided to lend 150 yuan to each household to cover the needs of building a room, to be repaid in four years with no interest. The loan will be disbursed in three installments: 50 yuan per installment. For the second and third installments, cash will be disbursed, but the municipal commissioner must first verify the housing construction situation of the household, mark it clearly, and then issue it. In order to prevent misuse in the first phase, a 50-yuan value voucher will be issued. The voucher will be divided into five coupons, each worth 10 yuan. Two coupons can be exchanged for cash for turnover, and three coupons must be exchanged for wood and water materials to prevent misuse. Still fearing that the supply of materials in rural areas will not meet the demand and that merchants will take the opportunity to monopolize them, Chairman Zhang Xiaoliang of the Lumber Association has been asked to provide materials at a fair price. The first batch of vouchers has been distributed successively since January 5 and will be redeemed soon. It is also heard that after the loans are repaid in the future, the bureau plans to transfer them to expand the original poverty alleviation lending office, so that it can still be used to actively alleviate poverty.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Asks Stamp Tax Bureau to Determine Stamp Application Period

Please Apply Stamps Starting from February 1

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Jiangsu Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau yesterday, stating: "To Whom It May Concern, on the 18th of this month, we received a letter from the Knitting Industry Association stating that we have received a letter from Jinghua Knitting Factory, a member of our association, stating that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce once announced that the closing period was the end of May and the end of September, and the end of January was the overall closing period. Businesses must change to new books every month after the overall closing period. We have received a reply from the Stamp Tax Bureau stating that if the aforementioned books are not exchanged for new books in January, stamps must be added to the old books, etc. It is difficult for the business community to change to new books before the overall closing period, and it is an unexpected burden to restamp books throughout the year, and there is no legal basis for it. We should transfer the request to determine the method, etc., and we have arrived at the Association. We have investigated that the closing date for the business community was changed last year to be held at the end of January of the following year by order of the Executive Yuan. The accounting year of the business community has been stipulated by the Yuan order, from February 1 of each year to the end of January of the following year. The period for adding new stamps to the books should also be based on this to connect with the year. Although the date is delayed by one month, there is no shortage of public tax revenue, and it is the result of complying with the Yuan's order and revising the date of the overall receipt. We should send a letter to your bureau to verify and reply, and transfer it to inspectors in each district to avoid misunderstandings. This is the purpose."

San You She Labor-Capital Dispute: National Government Orders Court Not to Accept Case

To Be Handled by Revised Labor Dispute Law

Municipal Party Headquarters Notifies Cotton Weavers' Union

The shutdown dispute at the San You Industrial Company in Pudong, Shanghai, was previously adjudicated by the Municipal Government in accordance with the law. However, the capital side refused to accept the ruling, causing delays for years without resolution. Subsequently, the Labor-Capital Dispute Handling Law was revised by the National Government and promulgated on September 27 of last year. According to the provisions of Article 7, Paragraph 1, of the law, neither the labor nor capital side may appeal the decision of the arbitration committee. Article 44, Paragraph 2, stipulates that disputes that occurred before the promulgation of the revised law but have not yet been resolved may be handled in accordance with this law. The labor side has therefore submitted a request to the Municipal Party Headquarters to find a way to prevent the capital side from appealing and to enforce the adjudication, based on the above provisions. The Municipal Party Headquarters replied to the Seventh District Cotton Weavers' Union yesterday, stating: "For the purpose of informing, we have investigated that the request from the union to the Jiangsu High Court to expedite the hearing of the labor-capital dispute over the shutdown of the Shanghai factory of the San You Industrial Company has been forwarded to the central government by this committee and approved on file. Now, we have received Public Letter No. 2570 from the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee, stating that the Labor-Capital Dispute Handling Law was revised and promulgated by the National Government on September 27 of this year. The labor-capital dispute of the San You Industrial Company should be handled in accordance with the new law. In accordance with the approval above, in addition to forwarding a letter to the Secretariat of the Central Committee to forward a letter to the National Government, instructing the Judicial Yuan to instruct the Jiangsu High Court to issue a ruling in accordance with the law that the case will not be accepted by either the labor or capital side, and separately notifying the Shanghai Municipal Government for reference, we hereby inform you that you are instructed to handle it in accordance with the law." Standing Committee Members Pan Gongzhan, Tong Xingbai, and Wu Xingya.

Clock Industry Promotes Domestic Goods

The clock industry in this city, taking merchants saving the nation as its principle, and only resisting foreign goods as the means, has on one hand notified fellow businesses to seal up all existing Japanese goods. It is heard that some are willing to destroy them voluntarily. On the other hand, it promotes domestic production, establishing factories for self-manufacturing, and notifying fellow businesses to vigorously promote sales. Because clock factories in other areas have traditionally had no contact with the association, their products and trademarks are unknown. It is heard that the association has sent letters to various factories inviting them to join, and has organized a branch association for promoting domestic goods. Its contents are extremely comprehensive. In addition to Chairman Chen Duoming also serving as the director of the branch association, Yan Boying has been elected as the head of the inspection section, Zhou Linxiang as the head of the investigation section, Sun Meitang as the head of the publicity section, and Li Weibao as the head of the research section. Each section has four staff members, all appointed by the executive committee. Now, we will transcribe the letter sent to various clock factories as follows:

Respectfully informing you, this association, considering the nation's difficulties worsening daily and now is the time for merchants to resist Japanese goods, domestic clocks have successively emerged. Although their factory locations are set up in other areas, their goods are actually transported to Shanghai for promotion. However, due to the constantly changing styles and trademarks, it is particularly difficult to distinguish them. In case unscrupulous individuals use counterfeits to confuse the genuine, and engage in price-cutting sales, it will inevitably affect domestic products. For prevention and promotion, all domestic factories within and outside this city should be notified to join this association as soon as possible, and promptly send the factory's products and trademarks to the association for circulation among fellow businesses, in order to identify them and prevent counterfeiting. This matter was submitted to the thirty-sixth executive committee meeting for discussion. Everyone agreed that if we don't do this we cannot resist the dumping of Japanese goods, and if we don't do this we cannot promote domestic goods that are just beginning to sprout. The resolution was passed and recorded. A corresponding record is enclosed, along with blank membership application forms and representative authorization forms, one copy each. These are sent along with this letter, hoping your factory will investigate and handle this accordingly, and reply is appreciated.

Stone Found in Cow's Abdomen

Guowenshe reports that Mr. Ma Qizhou, a famous chef in this city, purchased a cow's kidney yesterday morning intending to cook it for a meal. Upon dissection, he suddenly discovered objects inside the kidney that resembled neither stone nor bone, with multiple particles of varying sizes, the larger ones like hazelnuts, the smaller ones like beans. Their texture was hard and their color white, weighing over two qian (approximately 0.07 ounces). Furthermore, they had many gold specks, shining with five colors. According to the Compendium of Materia Medica, this is known as "Niu Huang" (cow gallstone). During the Gengzi year of Jiajing in the Ming Dynasty, the governor of Zhangzhou, Tu Dezhi, had no objections when a foreign monk claimed it was a precious treasure. Mongolians would soak the stone in water, play with it while chanting, and could pray for rain. Moreover, according to Jing Fang's "Book of Changes" divination, "When the army is strong and the ruler is martial, a stone will grow in the cow's abdomen." It is said to be a miraculous medicine for treating fright, toxins, and sores, similar to Gou Bao (dog gallbladder stone). However, the kidney is also a pure and empty organ, how could it produce a stone? Therefore, this is recorded in the hope that learned scholars will study it.
